Amm and Khass — General and Specific
beginner
6 min
Definitions of Khas and Amm in Usul al-Fiqh
Defining the specific and general terms in Quranic interpretation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define al-khas and al-amm with examples, and classify a given Quranic expression as specific or general.

Core Idea
Khas singles out one meaning; Amm covers many — both are foundational for deriving rulings.

The Qur'an contains both specific and general expressions. Understanding the difference between al-khas and al-amm is essential for correctly interpreting divine commands. In this lesson, you will learn the formal definitions provided by Imam al-Shashi, along with clear examples.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two key terms
Read the definitions of al-khas and al-amm. Note that khas is a word coined for a single known meaning, while amm covers a group of individuals.
2
Understand the three levels of Khas
Khas can specify an individual (like Zayd), a type (like man), or a genus (like human). Memorize these three categories.
3
Understand the two types of Amm
Amm can be by wording (like 'Muslims') or by meaning (like relative pronouns 'man' and 'ma'). Recognize both.
4
Apply the classification
Given a Quranic phrase, determine if it is khas or amm. Use the examples as a guide.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أربعة كتاب الله تعالى وسنة رسوله، وإجماع الأمة، والقياس، فلا بد من البحث في كل واحد من هذه الأقسام؛ ليعلم بذلك طريق تخريج الأحكام. البحث الأول في كتاب الله تعالى: فصل في الخاص والعام. فالخاص لفظ وضع لمعنى معلوم، أو المسمى معلوم على الانفراد، كقولنا: في تخصيص الفرد زيد، وفي تخصيص النوع: رجل، وفي تخصيص الجنس: إنسان. والعام: كل لفظ ينتظم جمعاً من الأفراد، إما لفظاً كقولنا: مسلمون، ومشركون. وإما معنى كقولنا: من وما.
Four: the Book of Allah Most High, the Sunnah of His Messenger, the consensus of the community, and analogical reasoning. So it is necessary to investigate each one of these categories to know thereby the method of deriving rulings. The first investigation: concerning the Book of Allah Most High: Chapter on the Specific and the General. The specific is an expression coined for a known meaning, or the named thing known singly, like our saying: in the specification of an individual: Zayd; in the specification of a type: man; in the specification of a genus: human. And the general is every expression that encompasses a grouping of individuals, either in wording like our saying: Muslims, polytheists; or in meaning like our saying: 'whoever' and 'whatever'.
Source pages p. 11

Commentary
This passage is the opening of the discussion on the specific and general in the Qur'an. The author first lists the four sources of Islamic law: the Qur'an, Sunnah, consensus, and analogy. Then he begins the first investigation focusing on the Qur'an, specifically the chapter on al-Khas and al-Amm. Al-Khas is defined as a word coined for a single known meaning, indicating one specific individual, type, or genus. For example, 'Zayd' is a specific individual, 'man' is a specific type, and 'human' is a specific genus. This classification helps in understanding how a text can apply to one or many. Al-Amm, on the other hand, is a word that encompasses a group of individuals, either explicitly like 'Muslims' or implicitly like relative pronouns 'man' (whoever) and 'ma' (whatever). These definitions are foundational for usul al-fiqh as they determine the scope of legal texts.

Key Terms
الخاص (al-khāṣṣ): A word coined for a single meaning, either a specific individual, a type, or a genus.
العام (al-ʿāmm): A word that encompasses a collection of individuals, either by wording or by meaning.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What are the three levels of specification (takhsis) mentioned in the definition of khas?
A) Individual, group, category
B) Individual, type, genus
C) Word, meaning, context
D) Singular, plural, collective

Key Takeaway
Khas singles out a specific meaning (individual, type, or genus), while Amm covers a group of individuals by wording or meaning.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
intermediate
8 min
The Binding Nature of Khas and Its Priority Over Zanni Proofs
Stating the ruling of a specific text when confronting zanni proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule for a khas text from the Quran and apply it when it conflicts with khabar wahid or qiyas.

Core Idea
A specific text from the Quran overrides any zanni proof unless reconciliation is possible without changing it.

In Hanafi usul, when a text is specific (khas), it carries definitive authority. But what happens when it meets a solitary report or an analogy? This lesson teaches the priority rule: the khas rules unless a harmonious reading is possible.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling of a khas text
Recognize that a khas from the Quran obligates acting upon it without fail (wajib al-'amal).
2
Check for conflict with zanni proofs
Determine if a khabar wahid or qiyas contradicts the khas. If yes, proceed to reconciliation attempt.
3
Attempt reconciliation without altering the khas
If the khabar wahid or qiyas can be interpreted in a way that does not change the specific ruling, both are acted upon.
This preserves both sources.
4
If reconciliation fails, give priority to the khas
When reconciliation is impossible, the khas prevails because it is qat'i, while the others are zanni.
The Book is left (meaning acted upon) and the conflicting proof is left (not acted upon).
5
Apply to the verse about 'iddah
The word 'three' is a specific number; any khabar wahid or qiyas that would change that number is rejected unless reconcilable.
This exemplifies the rule.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وحكم الخاص من الكتاب: وجوب العمل به لا محالة، فإن قابله خبر الواحد أو القياس، فإن أمكن الجمع بينهما بدون تغيير في حكم الخاص يعمل بهما، وإلا يعمل بالكتاب ويترك ما يقابله. مثاله: قوله تعالى: يَتَرَبَّصْنَ بِأَنْفُسِهِنَّ ثَلاثَةَ قُرُوءٍ فإن لفظة 'الثلاثة' خاص في تعريف عدد معلوم، فيجب العمل به.
The ruling of the specific from the Book: It is necessary to act upon it without fail. If a solitary report or analogy confronts it, then if it is possible to combine them without changing the ruling of the specific, both are acted upon; otherwise, one acts by the Book and leaves that which confronts it. Its example is His saying, the Most High: 'They shall wait for three quru''. For the word 'three' is specific in defining a known number, so it is obligatory to act upon it.
Source pages p. 12

Commentary
This passage establishes a fundamental principle in Hanafi usul: a specific text from the Qur'an (khas) is absolutely binding and must be acted upon unconditionally. When such a specific text is confronted by a solitary report (khabar wahid) or an analogy (qiyas), which are both probable (zanni) sources, the scholar must first attempt to reconcile them without altering the specific ruling. If reconciliation is possible, both are applied. If not, the specific text from the Book takes precedence because the Qur'an is qat'i (definitive), while khabar wahid and qiyas are only zanni. The example given is the famous verse about the 'iddah of women after divorce: they must wait for three quru'. The word 'three' is a specific number; therefore, it must be enforced as is. This ruling excludes the possibility of changing the waiting period based on a solitary report or analogy. The text does not discuss the meaning of 'quru' here; that is dealt with separately.

Key Terms
خبر الواحد (khabar al-wāḥid): A solitary report from the Prophet transmitted by one or few narrators, which is probable (zanni) in transmission.
قياس (qiyās): Analogical reasoning from a basis in the revealed sources, considered a probable source.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the ruling when a khas from the Qur'an is confronted by a khabar wahid?
A) The khas is set aside
B) Both are abandoned
C) First, attempt reconciliation; if not possible, the khas prevails
D) The khabar wahid takes precedence

Key Takeaway
A khas from the Quran is absolutely binding and overrides any zanni proof unless reconciliation is possible without changing the specific ruling.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
intermediate
10 min
Definition of Al-Amm and Ruling of Al-Khass
Defines 'amm and states ruling of acting upon khass

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define al-'amm, distinguish it from mushtarak and tathniyah, state the Hanafi ruling on acting upon a khass text from the Quran, and apply the rule of priority when khass conflicts with khabar wahid or qiyas.

Core Idea
The specific (khass) of the Quran is acted upon necessarily; it prevails over weaker evidence unless reconciliation is possible.

In this foundational lesson from Usul al-Shashi, we encounter the definition of al-'amm (the general) and the ruling of al-khass (the specific) from the Quran. The passage establishes that a specific Quranic text must be applied with certainty, and it outlines a hierarchy when such a text conflicts with a solitary hadith or analogy. Understanding this hierarchy is crucial for correct istinbat (derivation).

Guided Path
1
Define al-'amm
Identify the two types of 'amm: lafdhi (by wording, e.g., 'Muslimun') and ma'nawi (by meaning, e.g., 'man' and 'ma'). Note what is excluded: mushtarak (homonym), specific (khass), duals, and numbers.
The definition uses 'yantazim' to indicate comprehensive inclusion.
2
State the ruling of khass from the Quran
The ruling is wajib al-'amal bihi (obligatory to act upon) without exception. This is the position of the Iraqi school, al-Qadi Abu Zayd, and the two shaykhs.
This ruling assumes the khass is clear in meaning.
3
Introduce the conflict scenario
If a khass text is opposed by a khabar wahid (solitary report) or a zahir al-qiyas (apparent analogy), reconciliation is first attempted.
Reconciliation must not change the ruling of the khass.
4
Apply the reconciliation rule
If reconciliation is impossible without altering the khass, the Quranic khass prevails because it is qat'i (definitive) while the other sources are zanni (speculative).
The Quran is stronger due to certainty in transmission and meaning.
5
Recognize the epistemological dispute
The Hanafis hold that khass from the Quran gives qat'i knowledge. The Shafi'is and Samarqand scholars argue it gives only zanni knowledge due to the possibility of metaphorical interpretation. The Hanafi response uses the wall analogy: a mere possibility without evidence does not affect certainty.
This difference affects how conflicts are resolved.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
البحث الأول في كتاب الله
فصل في الخاص والعام
والعام: كُلُّ لفظ ينتظم جمعاً من الأفراد، إما لفظاً كقولنا: مسلمون، ومشركون. وإمّا معنى كقولنا: "مَنْ وَما".
وحكم الخاص من الكتاب: وجوب العمل به لا محالة، فإن قابله خبر الواحد أو عارضه ظاهر القياس، فإن أمكن الجمعُ بينهما بدون تغيير في حكم الخاص يعمل بهما، وإلا يعمل بالكتاب ويترك ما يقابله.
ينتظم: أي يشتمل احتراز عن المشترك؛ فإنه لا يشتمل معنيين أو أكثر، بل يحتمل كل واحد منهما على السوية بطريق البدلية. جمعاً: احتراز عن الخاص؛ فإنه ينتظم فرداً واحداً، وعن التثنية وأسماء الأعداد؛ لأنها ينتظم جمعاً أيضاً لكن من الأجزاء لا من الأفراد. وجوب العمل به إلخ : هذا مذهب مشايخ العراق والقاضي أبي زيد والشيخين ومن تابعهم؛ لأن المقصود من وضع الألفاظ للمعاني أن تدل عليها، وإلا لم تكن للوضع فائدة، وقال مشايخ سمرقند وأصحاب الشافعي الله لا يثبت الحكم به قطعاً؛ لأن كل لفظ يحتمل أن يراد به غير موضوعه مجازاً، والجواب منا: إن هذا الاحتمال لم ينشاء عن دليل، فلا يقدح في القطع، فمن قام تحت حائط لا ميل فيه لا يلام؛ لانتفاء دليل السقوط، بخلاف من قام تحته إذا كان فيه ميل؛ فإنه يلام لوجود دليل السقوط. وإلا يعمل بالكتاب لأن الكتاب أقوى منهما؛ لأنه قطعي وهما ظنيان؛ لأن في الخبر الواحد شبهة الانقطاع عنه عليه والقياس مبناه على الرأي وهو يحتمل الغلط.
The first research: concerning the Book of Allah. Chapter on the specific and the general. The general: every word that encompasses a collection of individuals, either in wording like 'Muslims' and 'polytheists', or in meaning like 'who' and 'what'. The ruling of the specific from the Book: obligation to act upon it necessarily. If it is opposed by a solitary report or by apparent analogy, then if reconciliation between them is possible without changing the ruling of the specific, both are acted upon; otherwise, the Book is acted upon and what opposes it is abandoned. 'Encompasses': i.e. includes, as a precaution against the homonym; for it does not include two or more meanings, but rather each one of them is equally probable by way of substitution. 'Collection': a precaution against the specific; for it encompasses a single individual, and against the dual and numbers; because they also encompass a collection but of parts not of individuals. 'Obligation to act upon it, etc.': This is the doctrine of the scholars of Iraq, al-Qadi Abu Zayd, the two shaykhs, and those who followed them, because the purpose of placing words for meanings is that they indicate them, otherwise there would be no benefit in the placing. The scholars of Samarqand and the followers of al-Shafi'i said: the ruling is not established definitively, because every word may be intended to mean other than its literal meaning metaphorically. Our response: this possibility did not arise from evidence, so it does not impair certainty. One who stands under a wall with no tilt is not blameworthy due to lack of evidence of falling, unlike one who stands under a wall with tilt; he is blameworthy due to existence of evidence of falling. 'Otherwise the Book is acted upon' because the Book is stronger than both; for it is definite and both are speculative, because in the solitary report there is the possibility of discontinuity from him (the Prophet), and analogy is based on opinion and is prone to error.
Source pages p. 12

Commentary
This passage begins the chapter on al-Khass (the specific) and al-Amm (the general) from Usul al-Shashi. It first defines 'amm as a word that encompasses a collection of individuals, either by its form (e.g., plural nouns) or by its meaning (e.g., 'who', 'what'). Then it states the ruling of khass from the Quran: it must be acted upon necessarily. However, if it conflicts with a solitary hadith (khabar wahid) or with apparent qiyas (analogy), the text explains that if reconciliation is possible without altering the khass, both are applied; otherwise, the Quranic khass prevails. This is because the Quran is qat'i (definitive) in both transmission and meaning, while khabar wahid and qiyas are zanni (speculative). The commentary elaborates on the definition, distinguishing 'amm from mushtarak (homonym) and from tathniyah (dual) and numbers. It also mentions a dispute: the scholars of Baghdad hold that khass from the Quran gives definitive knowledge, while the scholars of Samarqand and the Shafi'is disagree, arguing that any word can be interpreted metaphorically. The Hanafi response uses the analogy of a wall: a possibility without evidence does not affect certainty.

Key Terms
العام (al-'amm): Every word that encompasses a collection of individuals, either in wording (like Muslims) or in meaning (like man and ma).
الخاص (al-khass): A word that encompasses a single individual (implicitly opposed to 'amm).
خبر الواحد (khabar al-wahid): A solitary report, which is zanni (speculative) in transmission.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, what is the ruling on acting upon a specific (khass) text from the Quran if it conflicts with a solitary hadith?
A) The solitary hadith is preferred because it is from the Sunnah.
B) The specific text is acted upon unless reconciliation is impossible, in which case the Quran is preferred.
C) Both are abandoned and qiyas is used instead.
D) The specific text is considered abrogated by practice.

Key Takeaway
The khass of the Quran is acted upon necessarily; it is qat'i and prevails over zanni sources like khabar wahid and qiyas unless genuine reconciliation is possible.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific

Applying Khass: The 'Iddah Verse and the Quru' Dispute
Applies the usul principle of khass to two Quranic examples: the 'iddah verse and the mahr verse.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the khass element in Quran 2:228, apply the Hanafi principle of acting upon khass, and derive the fiqh ruling for 'iddah.

Core Idea
The word 'three' is khass (specific) and binding; the dispute over quru' determines the 'iddah period and many legal consequences.

The Quranic verse 'They shall wait for three quru'' provides a key example of how a specific (khass) text must be acted upon. The word 'three' fixes the number, but the meaning of 'quru'' is debated between menses and purity. This lesson unpacks the Hanafi position, its proof from the consensus of the Companions, and the far-reaching fiqh consequences that follow from this interpretation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the khass element
Find the word in the verse that indicates a specific number or quantity. This is the element that makes the text khass.
The verse says 'three quru'' — the word 'three' is a specific number.
2
Analyze the ambiguity of 'quru''
The term 'quru'' is a homonym (mushtarak) meaning both menstruation and purity. Determine which meaning each school adopts and their respective evidence.
Hanafis adopt menstruation based on consensus of the Four Caliphs and many Companions. Shafi'is adopt purity based on a linguistic argument.
3
Apply the rule 'al-khass yufidu al-wujub'
Since the text is khass, it is binding in its specific sense. The Hanafi interpretation of quru' as menstruation, combined with the specific number three, yields the ruling of three complete menstruations.
Acting upon the khass means accepting the number and the meaning determined by the stronger evidence.
4
Trace the thamarah al-khilaf
List the practical differences arising from the ikhtilaf: ruj'a in the third period, nafaqa, inheritance, etc. Understand how the same khass text leads to different rulings when the ambiguous term is resolved differently.
The Hanafi view allows ruj'a in the third menstruation; the Shafi'i view ends the 'iddah after two purities.
5
Examine the second example: mahr determination
The verse 'Qad 'alimna ma faradna' indicates that the mahr is legally determined (khass fi al-taqdir). The Hanafis hold a minimum of ten dirhams based on a hadith, while Shafi'is leave it to mutual consent.
This shows another type of khass: specific in legal valuation, not just number.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مثاله: في قوله تعالى: يَتَرَبَّصْنَ بِأَنْفُسِهِنَّ ثَلاثَةَ قُرُوءٍ فإن لفظة "الثلاثة" خاص في تعريف عدد معلوم، فيجب العمل به، ولو حُملَ "الأقراء" على الأطهار كما ذهب لا يحتمل الزيادة والنقصان. انتقص العدد الثلاثة من على كثيرين متفقين في الحكم الشرعي مثل رجل [الشافي: ص ۳۹] تخصيص الجنس: المراد من الجنس هنا: ما كان مشتملا على كثيرين متفاوتين في أحكام الشرع مثل: "إنسان"، ثم إن مما ينبغي أن يعلم أن تقسيم المصنف الله للخاص إنما هو عند الأصوليين لا عند المناطقة. [الشافي: ص ٣٩] ثلاثة قروء: جمع قرء، وهو مشترك بين الحيض والطهر، ولذلك اختلف فيه، فبعضهم أرادوا بها الحيض كما هو مذهبنا وهو قول الخلفاء الأربعة والعبادلة الثلاثة، وكثير من الصحابة له، وقال أحمد : كنت أقول بالأطهار ثم وقفت بقول الأكابر ، وبعضهم أرادوا بها الأطهار كما ذهب إليه الشافعي بالله، وهم كانوا أهل اللسان فثبت أنه مشترك، ودلائل الفريقين في المطولات لا تسعهما هذه الوريقات. عدد معلوم وهي الثلاثة الكوامل الأفراد، وإنما يعمل بها إذا أريد بها الحيض دون الطهر. إليه الشافعي له باعتبار أن الطهر مذكّر دون الحيض، وقد ورد الكتاب في الجمع بلفظ التأنيث، دلّ على أنه جمع المذكر وهو الطَّهر، لَزِمَ ترك العمل بهذا الخاص؛ لأن من حَمَله كَالشَّافِعِي على الطهر لا يوجب ثلاثة أطهار بل طهرين وبعض الثالث، وهو الذي وقع فيه الطلاق. الطهر وأي بعض الثالث يُحَرَّجُ على هذا حكم الرجعة في الحيضة الثالثة وزواله، وتصحيح نكاح الغير زوال حكمها عنده وإبطاله، وحكمُ الحَبس والإطلاق، والمسكن والإنفاق، والخلع والطلاق، وتزوج الزوج بأختها وأربع سواها، وأحكام الميراث مع كثرة تعدادها. وكذلك قوله تعالى: وَقَدْ عَلِمْنَا مَا فَرَضْنَا عَلَيْهِمْ فِي أَزْوَاجِهِمْ خاص في التقدير من المهور فيجب العمل به أي وإذا ثبت أنه خاص فيجب العمل به، وذلك إنما يتحقق إذا حمل الأقراء على الحيض؛ لأن طلاق السنة إنما يكون في الطهر، فإذا طلقها في الطهر يجب التربص بثلاثة حيض، فتصير العدة ثلاثة قرء كوامل فيخرج على هذا أي يستنبط ويتفرع على هذا الخلاف فيجوز الرجعة في الثالث عندنا لا عنده، ويصح فيه نكاح الغير عنده لختم العدة، لا عندنا، وتجلس بحبس العدة عندنا لا عنده، ويجب على الزوج السكنى والنفقة عندنا لبقاء العدة لا عنده، وكذا يصح إيقاع طلاق آخر والخلع في الثالث عندنا لبقاء العدة لا عنده، ولا يجوز فيه التزوج بأختها للزوم الجمع بين الأختين، وكذا تزوج أربع سواها للزوم الخمس به بالنظر إلى العدة عندنا لا عنده أحكام الميراث: فإذا مات الزوج في الحيضة الثالثة ورثت المطلقة وبطل لها الوصية عندنا لا عنده. قد علمنا أي قد علم الله ما يجب فرضه على المؤمنين في الأزواج كذا في "الكشاف"، وفي "التبيين" أي ما أوجبنا من المهور في أمتك في أزواجهم، ومن العوض في إمائهم. ما فرضنا فقوله تعالى: فَرَضْنَا خاص في التقدير الشرعي؛ لأنه أضاف الفرض وهو بمعنى التقدير إلى نفسه، فكان المهر مقدراً شرعاً بحيث لا يحوز النقصان منه إلا أنه في تعيين المقدار مجمل، فألحقت السنة بياناً له، ما وهي روى جابر بن عبد الله له عن النبي عليه أنه قال: لا النساء إلا الأولياء، ولا يزوجن إلا من الأكفاء، ولا لأقل من عشرة دراهم، وهو مذهب علي، وابن عمر وعائشة، وعامر ، وإبراهيم ، قال العيني: إذا روي مهر من طرق مفرداتها ضعيفة يصير حسناً ويحتج به على أن الاحتياط أيضاً في مذهبنا، وباقي الأحاديث إما مؤولة أو ضعيفة، فصارت العشرة تقديراً لازماً، والشافعي لم يجعله مقدراً بل جعله موكولاً إلى رأي الزوجين؛ لأنه بدل المعقود عليه وهو البضع، فصار كأعواض العقود المالية أي: البيع والإجارة وهو فيما يثبت على تراضي المتبايعين، فكذا هذا، لكنا نقول بهذا ترك الخاص من الكتاب فلا يصح.
Its example: In the saying of Allah Most High: 'They shall wait for three periods (quru')' – indeed the word 'three' is specific in defining a known number, so it is obligatory to act upon it. If 'quru'' is taken to mean purity as (some) held, it would not allow for increase or decrease. The number three (is) from many who agree on a legal ruling like a man. Specification of the genus: what is meant by genus here is what includes many differing in legal rulings like 'human'. Then it should be known that the author's division of the specific is only according to the usuliyyun, not the logicians. 'Three quru': plural of qar', which is a homonym between menstruation and purity, and thus there is disagreement. Some intended by it menstruation, which is our madhhab and the statement of the four caliphs, the three Abdullahs, and many companions. Ahmad said: I used to say purity, then I stopped at the statement of the great ones. Some intended by it purity as Imam al-Shafi'i held, and they were people of language, so it is established that it is a homonym. The proofs of the two groups are in lengthy works, not contained in these pages. A known number: the three complete individuals; it is only acted upon if menstruation is intended, not purity. Al-Shafi'i referred to the fact that purity is masculine while menstruation is feminine, and the Book came in the feminine plural, indicating that it is a plural of the masculine, which is purity. So one must abandon acting upon this specific; because one who takes it as purity does not obligate three purities but two purities and part of the third, which is the one in which divorce occurred. Purity and a part of the third. Upon this follow the rulings: the validity of return in the third menstruation and its nullification; the validity of marriage by another due to the end of the 'iddah according to him and its nullification; the rulings of detention and release, residence and spending, khul' and divorce, marriage with her sister and with four others, and the rulings of inheritance with their multiplicity. Likewise His saying: 'Indeed We have known what We have prescribed for them concerning their wives' is specific in the determination of dowries, so it is obligatory to act upon it. That is, if it is established that it is specific, then it is obligatory to act upon it. This is only realized if quru' is taken to mean menstruation, because the sunna divorce only occurs in a state of purity. So if she is divorced in purity, she must wait for three menstruations, so the 'iddah becomes three complete quru'. Then this (difference) is derived and branched: return is permissible in the third according to us, not according to him; marriage by another is valid according to him (due to end of 'iddah) not according to us; she remains in detention of 'iddah according to us, not according to him; the husband must provide housing and maintenance according to us (due to continuity of 'iddah), not according to him; likewise the pronouncement of another divorce and khul' are valid in the third according to us (due to continuity of 'iddah), not according to him; marriage with her sister is not permissible due to combining sisters; likewise marrying four others due to making five in view of the 'iddah according to us, not according to him. Rulings of inheritance: if the husband dies in the third menstruation, the divorced woman inherits and her will is nullified according to us, not according to him. 'Indeed We have known': i.e. Allah knows what He obligated upon the believers concerning wives as in al-Kashshaf, and in al-Tabyin: i.e. what We obligated of dowries in your nation for their wives, and of compensation for their slave girls. 'What We have prescribed': His saying 'faradna' is specific in legal determination; because He attributed obligation (which means determination) to Himself, so the dowry is legally determined such that it is not permissible to decrease from it, but it is ambiguous in specifying the amount, so the sunnah is attached as an explanation for it. It is narrated that Jabir ibn 'Abdullah (may Allah be pleased with him) reported from the Prophet (peace be upon him) that he said: 'No women (should be given in marriage) except by guardians, and they should not be married except to compatible men, and (the dowry) should not be less than ten dirhams.' This is the madhhab of 'Ali, Ibn 'Umar, 'A'isha, 'Amir, and Ibrahim. Al-'Ayni said: If a hadith about dowry is narrated through multiple weak chains, it becomes hasan and is used as evidence, and caution is also in our madhhab. The rest of the ahadith are either interpreted or weak, so the ten dirhams became a binding determination. Al-Shafi'i did not make it determined but made it subject to the spouses' opinion; because it is a compensation for the object of contract, which is the private part, so it is like compensations in financial contracts: sale and hire, which are based on the mutual agreement of the contracting parties. So this is similar. But we say: by this, the specific from the Book is abandoned, so it is not valid.
Source pages p. 12

Commentary
This passage provides a concrete example of the principle of acting upon a specific (khass) text. The Quranic verse 'They shall wait for three quru'' contains the word 'three', which is specific in number. The text explains that this specific must be acted upon, but the meaning of 'quru'' is disputed. The Hanafi position (followed by the four caliphs and many companions) is that quru' means menstruation (hayd). The Shafi'i position, based on linguistic arguments (since 'tuhur' is masculine and the plural is feminine), is that it means periods of purity (at-har). The passage then outlines the numerous fiqh implications from this dispute, including the permissibility of ruj'a in the third period, the status of 'iddah, financial obligations, and inheritance. The text then moves to another example: the verse 'Indeed We have known what We have prescribed for them concerning their wives' which is specific in indicating that the mahr (dowry) is fixed. The Hanafis hold that the mahr is legally determined (at least ten dirhams) based on a hadith, while the Shafi'is treat it as subject to mutual agreement. The passage argues that the Shafi'i view abandons the specific text of the Quran.

Key Terms
القرء (al-qar'): A homonym meaning both menstruation and purity; used in the verse for 'iddah.
خاص في التقدير (khass fi al-taqdir): A specific ruling regarding determination (e.g., the mahr is fixed).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Three complete menstrual periods.
B) Three complete purity intervals.
C) Two purity intervals and part of the third.
D) Until she gives birth.

Key Takeaway
The word 'three' in Quran 2:228 is khass and must be acted upon; the Hanafi interpretation of quru' as menstruation is based on consensus and practice, and it determines the entire 'iddah ruling and its numerous fiqh branches.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific

The Khass of 'Quru'': Grammatical and Legal Implications
Usul al-Shashi illustrates khass through the Quranic word 'quru''

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify a specific word (khass) in a Quranic text, analyze the grammatical indicators that determine its meaning, and derive the legal consequences that follow from two competing interpretations.

Core Idea
The meaning of 'quru'' is determined by its feminine grammatical form — a khass that carries extensive fiqh consequences.

The concept of khass (specific) is central to Hanafi usul al-fiqh. When a word in the Quran is specific, its meaning is binding unless a valid proof shifts it. This lesson examines the famous dispute over the word 'quru'' (Quran 2:228) between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools. The debate is not merely lexical; it branches out into a multitude of practical rulings on divorce, maintenance, and inheritance. By analyzing the grammatical form and its legal ramifications, we see how khass operates in usul al-fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the specific word (khass)
Locate the word 'quru'' in Quran 2:228. It is a plural form and the subject of a legal ruling regarding the 'iddah of divorced women.
The verse: 'And divorced women shall wait for three quru'.'
2
Analyze the grammatical indicator
The word 'thalathata' (three) is feminine. In Arabic, if 'quru'' were masculine (as in 'tuhr'), the masculine form 'thalathatu' would be required. Since 'thalathata' is feminine, 'quru'' must be feminine. The feminine noun for purity is 'hayd' (menstruation), not 'tuhr' (which is masculine).
This is a grammatical proof (dalil nahwi) that 'quru'' means hayd.
3
Compare with the Shafi'i interpretation
Al-Shafi'i argues that 'quru'' is the plural of 'qur'' (tuhr), and the feminine form is due to the feminine nature of the group or an exceptional usage. This requires ta'wil (interpretive shift) from the apparent meaning.
The Hanafi response is that such a ta'wil abandons the clear grammatical agreement.
4
Derive the Hanafi ruling
Since the khass is clear and no valid proof of ta'wil exists, the Hanafi position is that 'iddah consists of three complete menstrual cycles. This is binding on its instances.
This ruling is qat'i in the absence of a stronger counter-dalil.
5
Explore the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequences)
The difference leads to many furu': e.g., in the third menstruation, Hanafis allow raj'a (revocation of divorce) while Shafi'is do not; the 'iddah period ends at different times, affecting remarriage, inheritance, and maintenance.
The text lists rulings on marriage, shelter, khul', divorce, inheritance, etc.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في الخاص والعام
إليه الشافعي له باعتبار أن الطهر مذكّر دون الحيض، وقد ورد الكتاب في الجمع بلفظ التأنيث، دلّ على أنه جمع المذكر وهو الطَّهر، لَزِمَ ترك العمل بهذا الخاص؛ لأن من حَمَله كالشافعی على الطهر لا يوجب ثلاثة أطهار بل طهرين وبعض الثالث، وهو الذي وقع فيه الطلاق. الطهر وأي بعض الثالث يُحَرَّجُ على هذا حكم الرجعة في الحيضة الثالثة وزواله، وتصحيح نكاح الغير زوال حكمها عنده وإبطاله، وحكمُ الحَبس والإطلاق، والمسكن والإنفاق، والخلع والطلاق، وتزوج الزوج بأختها وأربع سواها، وأحكام الميراث مع كثرة تعدادها.
Section on the Specific and the General. To him, al-Shafi'i, because tuhr (purity) is masculine while hayd (menstruation) is feminine, and the Book came in the plural with the feminine suffix, indicating it is the plural of the masculine, i.e., tuhr. So it is necessary to abandon acting upon this specific (meaning) because whoever interprets it as al-Shafi'i does, i.e., as tuhr, does not require three tuhrs but rather two tuhrs and part of the third, which is the one in which divorce occurred. [This leads to] branching off from this: the ruling of taking back (raj'a) in the third menstruation and its lapse, the validity of marriage by another (in that period) according to him and its invalidation, the ruling of confinement and release, shelter and maintenance, khul' and divorce, marrying her sister and four others besides her, and the rulings of inheritance with their multiplicity.
Source pages p. 13

Commentary
This passage from Usul al-Shashi illustrates the concept of khass (specific) in Quranic language using the word 'quru'' (Quran 2:228). The author presents the Hanafi position that 'quru'' means menstruation (hayd), while al-Shafi'i interprets it as purity (tuhr). The dispute is not merely lexical; it has numerous fiqh consequences for 'iddah (waiting period) and divorce. Since the word appears in the feminine plural, and 'tuhr' is masculine while 'hayd' is feminine, the grammar supports the Hanafi view. The passage lists the practical differences: in the third menstruation, Hanafis permit raj'a (revocation of divorce), require shelter and maintenance, and do not consider the 'iddah complete, while Shafi'is do. These rules flow from whether the three 'quru'' are complete, which affects marriage, inheritance, and other rulings.

Key Terms
خاص (khass): A word that is specific in meaning, as opposed to general ('amm); it must be acted upon according to its specificity.
الأقراء (al-quru'): Plural of qur'; in this context, the 'iddah period for divorced women.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Three menstrual cycles.
B) Three periods of purity (tuhr).
C) Two menstrual cycles and part of a third.
D) Ninety days.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi interpretation of 'quru'' as menstruation is a classic application of khass (specific) in Quranic language, with far-reaching fiqh consequences that demonstrate the importance of grammatical analysis in usul al-fiqh.

The Khass of the Mahr Verse: When a Specific Text Overrides Analogy
Shows khass in the mahr verse and the dispute over its fixity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle that a khass text overrides qiyas by analyzing the dispute over the fixity of mahr and evaluating the Shafi'i counterargument.

Core Idea
A khass text in the Quran cannot be abandoned for a general analogy — the mahr is fixed by Shariah, not by mutual consent.

In this passage, the author continues to demonstrate the operation of khass texts in the Quran. The verse 'We have known what We have ordained for them concerning their wives' (Quran 33:50) uses the word 'faradna' (We ordained), which, according to Hanafi usul, indicates a fixed legal estimation. However, the Shafi'i school argues that mahr is like a price in a sale, left to agreement. The core usul question is: can qiyas override a khass text? Let's dissect the arguments.

Guided Path
1
Identify the khass element in the verse
Locate the word 'faradna' (We ordained) and note that it is attributed to Allah, indicating a specific divine estimation. This makes the verse khass regarding the estimation of mahr.
Khass is a text that indicates a specific ruling on a specific subject, and must be acted upon according to Hanafi usul.
2
Understand the Hanafi claim
Because the verse is khass, it mandates that the mahr is fixed by Shariah. The Hanafi school holds that the minimum mahr is ten dirhams based on a hadith from Jabir.
The hadith is used to clarify the ambiguous (mujmal) amount, not to override the khass.
3
Understand the Shafi'i analogy
Imam al-Shafi'i analogizes mahr to the price in a sale: since both are compensations for a right, they should be determined by mutual consent. He thus denies a fixed minimum.
The analogy is based on the general principle that financial contracts are based on consent.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response is that this analogy 'abandons the khass of the Book' — a specific text cannot be overridden by a general analogy. The hadith specifying ten dirhams is considered sound and is used to fix the minimum.
The principle here is that khass is qat'i (definitive) in its application, while qiyas is zanni (speculative).
5
Trace the furu' (branches)
The passage lists several consequences that follow from the Shafi'i view, such as permitting triple talaq in one sitting and allowing khul' as annulment. These are rejected by Hanafis because they contradict specific texts.
This shows how a single usul difference (khass vs qiyas) can affect multiple fiqh rulings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكذلك قوله تعالى: وَقَدْ عَلِمْنَا مَا فَرَضْنَا عَلَيْهِمْ فِي أَزْوَاجِهِمْ خاص في التقدير من المهور فيجب العمل به أي وإذا ثبت أنه خاص فيجب العمل به، وذلك إنما يتحقق إذا حمل الأقراء على الحيض؛ لأن طلاق السنة إنما يكون في الطهر، فإذا طلقها في الطهر يجب التربص بثلاثة حيض، فتصير العدة ثلاثة قرء كوامل فيخرج على هذا أي يستنبط ويتفرع على هذا الخلاف فيجوز الرجعة في الثالث عندنا لا عنده، ويصح فيه نكاح الغير عنده لختم العدة، لا عندنا، وتجلس بحبس العدة عندنا لا عنده، ويجب على الزوج السكنى والنفقة عندنا لبقاء العدة لا عنده، وكذا يصح إيقاع طلاق آخر والخلع في الثالث عندنا لبقاء العدة لا عنده، ولا يجوز فيه التزوج بأختها للزوم الجمع بين الأختين، وكذا تزوج أربع سواها للزوم الخمس به بالنظر إلى العدة عندنا لا عنده أحكام الميراث: فإذا مات الزوج في الحيضة الثالثة ورثت المطلقة وبطل لها الوصية عندنا لا عنده. قد علمنا أي قد علم الله ما يجب فرضه على المؤمنين في الأزواج كذا في "الكشاف"، وفي "التبيين" أي ما أوجبنا من المهور في أمتك في أزواجهم، ومن العوض في إمائهم. ما فرضنا فقوله تعالى: فَرَضْنَا خاص في التقدير الشرعي؛ لأنه أضاف الفرض وهو بمعنى التقدير إلى نفسه، فكان المهر مقدراً شرعاً بحيث لا يحوز النقصان منه إلا أنه في تعيين المقدار مجمل، فألحقت السنة بياناً له، ما وهي روى جابر بن عبد الله له عن النبي عليه أنه قال: لا النساء إلا الأولياء، ولا يزوجن إلا من الأكفاء، ولا لأقل من عشرة دراهم، وهو مذهب علي، وابن عمر وعائشة، وعامر ، وإبراهيم ، قال العيني: إذا روي مهر من طرق مفرداتها ضعيفة يصير حسناً ويحتج به على أن الاحتياط أيضاً في مذهبنا، وباقي الأحاديث إما مؤولة أو ضعيفة، فصارت العشرة تقديراً لازماً، والشافعي لم يجعله مقدراً بل جعله موكولاً إلى رأي الزوجين؛ لأنه بدل المعقود عليه وهو البضع، فصار كأعواض العقود المالية أي: البيع والإجارة وهو فيما يثبت على تراضي المتبايعين، فكذا هذا، لكنا نقول بهذا ترك الخاص من الكتاب فلا يصح. الشرعي، فلا يُترَكُ العَمَلُ به باعتبار أنه عقد مالي فيعتبر بالعقود المالية، فيكون تقدير أي النكاح المال فيه موكولاً إلى رأي الزوجين كما ذكره الشافعي حاله. مفوضاً وفرَّع على هذا: ۱- أن التخلّي لنفل العبادة أفضل من الاشتغال بالنكاح. ٢- وأباح الشافعي إبطاله بالطلاق كيف ما شاء الزوج من جمع وتفريق. - وأباح إرسال الثلاث جملة الشافعي النكاح واحدة. ٤ - وجعل عقد النكاح قابلا للفسخ بالخلع. الشافعي الطلقات
And likewise His saying: 'And We have known what We have ordained for them concerning their wives' is specific (khass) in the estimation of dowries. So it is necessary to act upon it. That is, if it is established that it is specific, then it must be acted upon. That is realized only if 'quru'' is interpreted as menstruation... [then repeats the same furu' from lesson 1]. 'We have known' means Allah has known what must be prescribed for the believers regarding spouses, as in al-Kashshaf, and in al-Tabyin: 'what We have imposed of dowries in your nation regarding their spouses and of compensation regarding their slave women.' 'What We have prescribed' (faradna) is specific (khass) in the legal estimation because He attributed the prescription (farad), which means estimation, to Himself, so the dowry is legally estimated such that it cannot be reduced, except that the amount is ambiguous (mujmal), so the Sunnah provided clarification. It is narrated from Jabir ibn Abdullah from the Prophet (ﷺ) that he said: 'No women [are married] except through guardians, and they should not be married except to suitable matches, and [the dowry should] not be less than ten dirhams.' This is the view of Ali, Ibn Umar, Aisha, 'Amir, and Ibrahim. al-Ayni said: If the hadiths about the dowry are narrated through chains that are individually weak, they become hasan and can be used as proof, and caution (ihtiyat) also supports our madhhab. The other hadiths are either interpreted or weak. Thus ten dirhams became a fixed estimation. Al-Shafi'i did not make it fixed but left it to the discretion of the spouses, because it is the compensation for the object of the contract (al-bud'), so it becomes like compensations in financial contracts, i.e., sale and lease, which are based on mutual consent. So similarly here. But we say: this abandons acting on the specific (khass) text of the Book, so it is not valid. [The argument about] legal (estimation) is not abandoned because it is a financial contract, so it is analogized to financial contracts, making the estimation of the wealth in marriage subject to the spouses' opinion as al-Shafi'i stated. [He] delegated it and branched off from this: (1) that devotion to supererogatory worship is better than engaging in marriage; (2) al-Shafi'i permitted annulment (of marriage) by divorce however the husband wishes, whether in combination or separation; (3) he permitted sending three divorces in one sentence; (4) he made the marriage contract subject to annulment by khul'. [al-Shafi'i on the divorces].
Source pages p. 13

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion of khass with another Quranic example: 'qad 'alimna ma faradna 'alayhim fi azwajihim' (Quran 33:50). The author argues that the word 'faradna' (We have ordained) makes the dowry a specific estimation, so it is fixed by Shariah. However, the amount is not specified in the Quran, so the Sunnah clarifies it as a minimum of ten dirhams, citing a hadith from Jabir. Al-Shafi'i disagrees, viewing the dowry as a financial consideration like in sale, left to mutual agreement. The Hanafi response is that this would abandon the khass import of the verse. The passage then lists several furu' that follow from the Shafi'i analogy of marriage to financial contracts: preference for celibacy over marriage, unrestricted divorce, triple talaq in one sitting, and khul' as annulment. The Hanafi position is that these rulings contradict the specific textual indications.

Key Terms
خاص (khass): Specific textual indication that must be acted upon.
المهر (al-mahr): The dowry given by the husband to the wife in marriage.
التقدير الشرعي (al-taqdir al-shar'i): Legal estimation or determination by Shariah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
A specific Quranic text (khass) cannot be overridden by a general analogy (qiyas); the mahr is fixed by Shariah, not by mutual agreement.

The Khass of the Marriage Verse: Restriction and Ikhtilaf
Analyzes the khass nature of the marriage verse and subsequent madhhab differences

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the khass in the marriage verse and apply the Hanafi principle to determine the requirement of a wali.

Core Idea
A verse can be khass yet still be interpreted differently due to different views on restriction by ahad hadith.

This passage from al-Shashi's Usul presents the verse 'until she marries another husband' as an example of khass. It then shows how the Hanafi school handles the apparent conflict between this verse and the hadith requiring a guardian, and contrasts it with the Shafi'i approach. Additionally, it records the internal Hanafi differences among the three imams. This lesson will guide you through the usul reasoning behind these positions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the khass text
Locate the verse 'حَتَّى تَنْكِحَ زَوْجاً غَيْرَهُ' and note that it is specific (khass) to the woman's act of marrying another husband.
2
Understand the Hanafi handling of the contradicting hadith
See how the Hanafi authors cite the hadith 'Any woman who marries without a guardian, her marriage is void' and argue that it is not mutawatir, so it cannot override the qat'i Quranic text. Instead, the hadith is interpreted as a recommendation.
3
Contrast with the Shafi'i approach
Al-Shafi'i analogizes marriage to financial contracts (qiyas) and takes the hadith literally, requiring a guardian. Identify the different usul principles at play.
4
Analyse internal Hanafi ikhtilaf
Observe the positions of Abu Hanifa (valid without wali), Muhammad (mawquf), and Abu Yusuf (initially required, then retracted). Note which is mufta bihi.
5
Apply the concept of khass
Derive the ruling for a modern scenario: a mature Hanafi woman marrying without a wali. Use the chain: [verse as khass] → [Hanafi principle: khass is qat'i] → [hadith is zanni, reinterpreted] → [woman may marry herself].

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكذلك قوله تعالى: ﴿ حَتَّى تَنْكِحَ زَوْجاً غَيْرَهُ خاص في وجود النكاح من المرأة، فلا مثل قوله: فرضنا يترك العمل به بما روي عن النبي علي "أيما امرأة نَكَحَتْ نفسها بغير إذن وليها كابنها وأبيها وأخيها فنكاحُها باطل باطل باطل" وفرع على هذا أي فرع الشافعي له هذه الأشياء المذكورة على قاعدة "النكاح عقد يجري مجرى العقود المالية". [الشافي: ٤٢] أفضل لأن النكاح من المعاملات كسائر العقود المالية، ونحن نتمسك بسنته صلى الله عليه وسلم حيث اختاره على التخلي مع ما ورد منه الحث عليه باكد أمر بألفاظ مختلفة، والاعتصام بهديه عليه أولى من اختيار سيرة يحيى بن زكريا عليه من جمع وتفريق: فالجمع: أن يوقع ثلاثاً في طهر واحد، والتفريق: أن يفرق الثلاث في ثلاثة أطهار، ويباح إرسال الثلاث جملة أي دفعة واحدة، وبلفظ واحد كما جاز فسخ البيع مطلقاً، وعندنا الجمع بين الطلقتين والثلاث في طهر واحد، أو كلمة واحدة بدعة؛ لأنه مخالف السنة؛ لأن النكاح سنة يتعلق به المصالح الدينية والدنيوية، فيكره إبطاله إلا على قدر الحاجة إلى الخلاص. في وجود النكاح: قال أبو حنيفة لله يجوز إنكاحها نفسها بالغة بغير ولي، وقال محمد الله: ينعقد موقوفاً، وعن أبي يوسف له لا ينعقد إلا بولي، ثم رجع وقال: ينعقد مطلقا، ويروى رجوع محمد الله إلى قولهما، رواه أبو داود رقم: ۲۰۸۳، باب في الولي، والترمذي رقم: ۱۱۰۲، باب ما جاء لا نكاح إلا بولي، وقال الترمذي: هذا حديث حسن، وابن ماجه رقم: ۱۸۷۹، باب لا نكاح إلا بولي، وأحمد رقم ٢٤٢٥١ ، ٢٤٤١٧ ، والحاكم في مستدركه ١٦٨/٢ ، والدارمي في باب النهي عن النكاح بغير ولي، عن عائشة لها .
And likewise His saying: 'until she marries another husband' is specific (khass) in the existence of marriage from the woman. So it is not like His saying 'We have ordained' that one should abandon acting upon it because of what is narrated from the Prophet (ﷺ): 'Any woman who marries herself without the permission of her guardian — whether her son, father, or brother — her marriage is void, void, void.' And al-Shafi'i branched off from this based on the principle 'marriage is a contract that follows the course of financial contracts.' [Al-Shafi'i: 42] Better because marriage is from transactions like other financial contracts. And we adhere to his Sunnah (ﷺ) because he chose it over celibacy, along with his emphatic encouragement in different wordings. Clinging to his guidance is better than choosing the way of Yahya ibn Zakariyya (upon him peace). [Discussion of] combination (jam') and separation (tafriq): Combination is to pronounce three divorces in one tuhr; separation is to separate the three across three tuhrs. He permitted sending the three together, i.e., at once, and in one utterance, just as annulment of sale is permitted absolutely. In our view, combining two or three divorces in one tuhr or in one word is an innovation (bid'a) because it contradicts the Sunnah; because marriage is a Sunnah connected to religious and worldly interests, so its annulment is disliked except to the extent of necessity for deliverance. Regarding the existence of marriage: Abu Hanifa (may Allah be pleased with him) said: A mature woman may marry herself without a guardian. Muhammad (may Allah be pleased with him) said: It is concluded but held in abeyance (mawquf). And it is narrated from Abu Yusuf (may Allah be pleased with him) that it is not valid except with a guardian, then he retracted and said it is valid absolutely. And it is reported that Muhammad retracted to their view. [Narrated by] Abu Dawud (no. 2083), al-Tirmidhi (no. 1102, who said it is hasan), Ibn Majah (no. 1879), Ahmad (nos. 24251, 24417), al-Hakim in his Mustadrak (2/168), and al-Darimi, from A'ishah (may Allah be pleased with her).
Source pages p. 14

Commentary
This passage presents the third example of khass: the Quranic verse 'until she marries another husband' (Quran 2:230) is khass in its application to the woman's act of marriage. The Hanafi position is that this khass is restricted by the hadith requiring a guardian for a woman's marriage. Al-Shafi'i, however, analogizes marriage to financial contracts, which does not require a guardian. The passage then lists Shafi'i's furu': preference for celibacy, permissibility of triple talaq, etc., which Hanafis reject as contrary to the Sunnah. Notably, the passage records internal Hanafi differences: Abu Hanifa holds that a mature woman can marry without a guardian (the marriage is valid), Muhammad says it is mawquf (suspended pending approval), and Abu Yusuf initially required a guardian but later retracted. This illustrates that ikhtilaf exists within the madhhab as well, but the relied-upon position is that of Abu Hanifa.

Key Terms
خاص (khass): A specific textual indication that requires action; in this context, the verse is khass because it specifically addresses the woman's marriage after divorce.
النكاح (al-nikah): Marriage contract; considered a religious act (ibadah) and also has transactional elements.
الولي (al-wali): Guardian who has authority over the woman's marriage.
معلوم (ma'lum): Known; in the text, the hadith is transmitted as 'hasan' but is not mutawatir.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, how is the hadith 'No marriage without a guardian' interpreted?
A) It is taken literally and abrogates the Quranic verse.
B) It is interpreted as a recommendation (nadb) because the Quranic text is qat'i.
C) It is rejected entirely as a fabrication.
D) It is applied only if the woman is a minor.

Key Takeaway
The khass verse is qat'i and cannot be overridden by an ahad hadith, leading to the Hanafi ruling that a woman may marry without a guardian.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
intermediate
8 min
Khass: Specific Texts Override General Analogy
Explains the concept of khass using nikah examples.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify a khass text in the Quran or Sunnah and explain why the Hanafi school applies it literally, rejecting any general analogy.

Core Idea
A specific text (khass) is applied as stated; it cannot be overridden by qiyas.

The Hanafi school holds that when a text is specific (khass), it must be applied exactly as stated, even if a general analogy suggests a different ruling. This lesson examines the dispute over whether marriage is analogous to a financial contract. We will analyze two key texts: the Quranic verse 'until she marries another husband' and the hadith on marriage without a guardian. The lesson demonstrates the priority of khass over qiyas.

Guided Path
1
Identify the khass texts in the passage
Locate the Quranic verse and the hadith. They are both specific in their scope—one refers to the woman's marriage, the other to the requirement of a guardian.
The hadith uses repetition for emphasis: 'bāṭil bāṭil bāṭil'.
2
Classify the texts according to Hanafi usul
Both are khass, meaning they apply to their specific subjects without generality. The Hanafi rule is that khass is qat'ī in its application.
Shafi'is also consider them khass but allow overriding via qiyas.
3
Apply the Hanafi principle: khass cannot be abandoned for qiyas
Even though marriage involves a financial element (mahr), the explicit text takes precedence over the financial analogy.
This is the core point of the dispute.
4
Derive the ruling on marriage without a guardian
From the hadith, the literal ruling is that the marriage is invalid without a guardian. However, Hanafi imams differ on its application to mature women.
Abu Hanifa allows it; Muhammad and Abu Yusuf have varying positions.
5
Note the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
The dispute affects the validity of triple divorce in one sitting and the need for a guardian.
Shafi'i allows triple divorce; Hanafi considers it bid'ah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في الخاص والعام
الشرعي، فلا يُترَكُ العَمَلُ به باعتبار أنه عقد مالي فيعتبر بالعقود المالية، فيكون تقدير أي النكاح المال فيه موكولاً إلى رأي الزوجين كما ذكره الشافعي حاله.
وفرَّع على هذا: ١- أن التخلّي لنفل العبادة أفضل من الاشتغال بالنكاح. ٢- وأباح الشافعي إبطاله بالطلاق كيف ما شاء الزوج من جمع وتفريق. ٣- وأباح إرسال الثلاث جملة واحدة. ٤- وجعل عقد النكاح قابلا للفسخ بالخلع.
وكذلك قوله تعالى: ﴿ حَتَّى تَنْكِحَ زَوْجاً غَيْرَهُ﴾ خاص في وجود النكاح من المرأة، فلا يُترَكُ العمل به بما روي عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم: "أيما امرأة نَكَحَتْ نفسها بغير إذن وليها كابنها وأبيها وأخيها فنكاحُها باطل باطل باطل"
وفرع على هذا أي فرع الشافعي له هذه الأشياء المذكورة على قاعدة: "النكاح عقد يجري مجرى العقود المالية". أفضل لأن النكاح من المعاملات كسائر العقود المالية، ونحن نتمسك بسنته صلى الله عليه وسلم حيث اختاره على التخلي مع ما ورد منه الحث عليه بأكد أمر بألفاظ مختلفة، والاعتصام بهديه عليه أولى من اختيار سيرة يحيى بن زكريا عليه السلام. من جمع وتفريق: فالجمع: أن يوقع ثلاثاً في طهر واحد، والتفريق: أن يفرق الثلاث في ثلاثة أطهار، ويباح إرسال الثلاث جملة أي دفعة واحدة، وبلفظ واحد كما جاز فسخ البيع مطلقاً، وعندنا الجمع بين الطلقتين والثلاث في طهر واحد، أو كلمة واحدة بدعة؛ لأنه مخالف السنة؛ لأن النكاح سنة يتعلق به المصالح الدينية والدنيوية، فيكره إبطاله إلا على قدر الحاجة إلى الخلاص. في وجود النكاح: قال أبو حنيفة رضي الله عنه: يجوز إنكاحها نفسها بالغة بغير ولي، وقال محمد رضي الله عنه: ينعقد موقوفاً، وعن أبي يوسف رضي الله عنه: لا ينعقد إلا بولي، ثم رجع وقال: ينعقد مطلقاً، ويروى رجوع محمد رضي الله عنه إلى قولهما.
ويتفرع منه: الخلاف في حلّ الوَطْء، ولزوم المهر، والنفقة، والسكنى، ووقوع الطلاق، والنكاح بعد الطلقات الثلاث على ما ذهب إليه قدماء أصحابه، بخلاف ما اختاره المتأخرون منهم.
Chapter on the Specific and the General. Legal (text) is not abandoned on the basis that it is a financial contract, so it is considered by financial contracts, so its estimation—that is, the wealth in marriage—is delegated to the opinion of the spouses as al-Shafi'i mentioned. And he derived from this: 1. Devotion to supererogatory worship is better than occupying oneself with marriage. 2. Al-Shafi'i permitted annulling it by divorce however the husband wishes, whether combined or separated. 3. He permitted sending three (divorces) all together. 4. He made the marriage contract subject to annulment by khul'. Similarly, the Almighty's saying: "until she marries another husband" is specific to the occurrence of marriage from the woman, so it is not abandoned by what is narrated from the Prophet (peace be upon him): "Any woman who marries herself without the permission of her guardian—like her son, her father, and her brother—her marriage is invalid, invalid, invalid." And he derived from this—al-Shafi'i derived these mentioned things on the basis: "Marriage is a contract that runs the course of financial contracts." It is better because marriage is from transactions like all other financial contracts, and we adhere to his Sunnah (peace be upon him) where he chose it over seclusion, along with what has come from him of encouragement with emphatic command in different wordings, and adhering to his guidance is better than choosing the way of Yahya ibn Zakariyya (peace be upon him). Regarding accumulation and separation: accumulation means to pronounce three (divorces) in one pure period, separation means to separate them over three pure periods, and it is permissible to send the three all together—i.e., at once—with a single word, just as annulment of sale is absolutely permitted. With us, combining two or three divorces in one pure period or in one word is an innovation (bid'a) because it is contrary to the Sunnah; because marriage is a Sunnah connected to religious and worldly interests, so annulling it is disliked except to the extent of need for deliverance. Regarding the occurrence of marriage: Abu Hanifa (may Allah be pleased with him) said: A mature woman may marry herself without a guardian; Muhammad (may Allah be pleased with him) said: It is concluded with suspension; from Abu Yusuf (may Allah be pleased with him): It is not concluded except with a guardian, then he retracted and said: It is concluded absolutely, and it is narrated that Muhammad (may Allah be pleased with him) retracted to their view. From this derives the dispute over the permissibility of intercourse, the obligation of the dowry, maintenance, housing, the occurrence of divorce, and marriage after three divorces according to what his earlier companions held, contrary to what the later ones chose.
Source pages p. 14

Commentary
This passage deals with the concept of khass (specific) in usul al-fiqh, using the example of marriage and divorce. The author begins by discussing al-Shafi'i's view that marriage is analogous to a financial contract, and then lists four derivations from that principle: (1) supererogatory worship is better than marriage, (2) divorce can be pronounced in any manner, (3) three divorces can be sent together, and (4) marriage can be annulled by khul'. The author then presents the Quranic verse "until she marries another husband" as a khass text that is applied specifically to the woman's marriage. This khass should not be overridden by a hadith about a woman marrying without a guardian—the author argues that the hadith is also khass and must be applied as is. The author then reports the Hanafi position: Abu Hanifa allows a mature woman to marry without a guardian, Muhammad holds it is suspended, Abu Yusuf initially required a guardian but later retracted. The dispute has practical consequences for the validity of intercourse, dowry, etc. The Hanafi school prioritizes the explicit text over analogical reasoning from financial contracts.

Key Terms
خاص (khass): A text that specifies a particular individual or limited category, applied exactly as stated.
قياس (qiyas): Analogical deduction used to extend a ruling from an original case to a new case based on a shared effective cause.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the primary reason for not equating marriage with a financial contract like sale?
A) Marriage involves religious and social interests beyond mere property.
B) The Quran explicitly says marriage is not a financial contract.
C) The Prophet forbade analogizing marriage to sale.
D) There is no hadith on the matter.

Key Takeaway
Khass texts are applied literally even if a general analogy suggests a different ruling; marriage is not analogous to financial contracts because of its specific nature.

Marriage Contract Dispute: Hanafi vs. Shafi'i on Qiyas and Khass
Explains the dispute over the nature of marriage contract.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on marriage as a non-financial contract and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument based on qiyas.

Core Idea
Marriage is a religious contract; explicit texts (khass) override financial analogies.

This lesson delves into the inter-madhhab dispute between Hanafi and Shafi'i over the nature of marriage. The Shafi'i school analogizes marriage to financial contracts, leading to permissive rulings on divorce and annulment. The Hanafi school, citing specific texts and the Sunnah, treats marriage as a unique contract with religious dimensions. We will examine the proofs from both sides and the practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position on marriage
Marriage is a religious contract (sunnah) with spiritual and social benefits; it is not purely financial.
The Prophet chose marriage over seclusion.
2
Identify the Shafi'i position
Marriage is like a financial contract because it involves mahr and property, so it should be governed by the same rules as sale.
This leads to four practical consequences listed in the passage.
3
Analyze the Shafi'i proof: qiyas
They analogize marriage to sale based on the presence of financial consideration.
The 'illa is the financial element.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response: khass texts and Sunnah
The Prophet's practice and specific texts (hadith on guardian) take precedence over analogy.
The Quranic verse is also khass.
5
Apply the thamarah al-khilaf
Differences in permissibility of triple divorce, need for guardian, and annulment by khul'.
Hanafi considers triple divorce in one sitting bid'ah.

بدعة (bid'a): An innovation in religious matters that contradicts the Sunnah.

D) Because the Quran explicitly forbids it.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school resists analogizing marriage to sale because specific texts and the Prophetic Sunnah establish marriage as a distinct religious contract.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific

'Amm: Definition, Types, and Epistemological Status
Defines 'amm and its two types, discusses its epistemological weight and cross-madhhab dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define 'amm (general), classify it into its two types, and explain why the Hanafi school holds that 'amm is qat'i (definitive) in the absence of takhsis, contrasting it with the Shafi'i view.

Core Idea
The general ('amm) is definitive (qat'i) until proven otherwise — specification is an exception, not the rule.

This lesson introduces the concept of 'amm (general) in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. You will learn the two types of 'amm and the crucial epistemological debate: is a general text certain or probable? The Hanafi school, particularly the Iraq mashayikh, holds that 'amm is qat'i, a stance that affects how Quranic and hadith texts are applied. This principle has real consequences for deriving rulings, such as whether a solitary hadith can specify a general Quranic verse.

Guided Path
1
Define 'amm and identify its two types
Read the opening lines: 'amm is a word that includes all individuals of its category, and it is of two types: one from which some individuals have been specified, and one from which nothing has been specified.
This classification is foundational for understanding how general texts are treated in usul.
2
Locate the epistemological dispute
The passage discusses different views: Ash'aris suspend judgment, some (al-Thalji) hold partial certainty, but the majority of Hanafis (Iraq mashayikh and later scholars) hold that 'amm is qat'i, while Shafi'i and most jurists/theologians hold it is zanni.
Identify each position and its proponents.
3
Understand the Hanafi proof for qat'i
The Hanafi position is based on linguistic usage and the practice of the Salaf, who acted on general texts without hesitation until a specifier appeared.
Specification is an exception; the default is generality.
4
Contrast with the opposing view and identify the thamarah
The Shafi'i view holds that 'amm is zanni because many general texts have been specified. The practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) is whether a general Quranic text can be specified by a solitary hadith or analogy; Hanafi allows it, Shafi'i generally does not.
This affects the hierarchy of evidence.
5
Note the tarjih (preferred view)
The author states that the view of the Iraq mashayikh (qat'i) is the mukhtar among the Samarqand mashayikh, though there is a difference within Hanafism.
Later Hanafi fatwa relies on the qat'i view.

Source Text

وأما العام فنوعان : ١- عام خُص عنه البعض -٢- وعام لم يخص عنه شيء، فالعام أي بعض أفراده
وروى الحسن عن أبي حنيفة رحمه الله: ينعقد في الكفؤ لا في غيره، ومثله عن أبي يوسف رحمه الله و به أخذ أكثر المشايخ وهو المختار للفتوى وقال مالك والشافعي رحمهما الله: لا ينعقد بعبارتهن.
أيما إلخ: هو من حديث عائشة مرفوعاً، وفي آخره: "فنكاحها باطل فنكاحها باطل فنكاحها باطل، فإن دخل بها فلها المهر بما استحل من فرجها، فإن اشتجروا فالسلطان ولي من لا ولي له" أخرجه الشافعي وأحمد وأبو داود والترمذي وحسنه وابن ماجه وأبو عوانة والطحاوي والحاكم وابن حبان، وله وجوه آخر، ولنا أيضاً وجوه إن شئت الإطلاع عليهما فليرجع إلى المطولات.
باطل باطل إلخ والتكرار لدفع التجوز وهو أن يراد بالباطل غير الكامل، أو لاهتمام المتكلم بالمعنى المدلول عليه، أقول: إن التكرار ثلاث مرات على ما يفهم من عبارة الخيالي يكون في موضع العتاب والزجر كما في قوله عليه السلام: "أي عبد تزوج بغير إذن مولاه فهو عاهر عاهر عاهر" أي زان؛ لتمرده على مولاه بإنكاح نفسه بغير إذنه، وكذا قوله عليه السلام في السرقة: "فإن عاد فاقطعوه فاقطعوه"، فقوله عليه السلام: أي امرأة إلخ من هذا القبيل. [عمدة الحواشي ص: ١٦-١٧] ويتفرع منه من أن النكاح ينعقد بعبارة النساء. والنكاح: أي إذا طلق الزوج ثلاثاً هذه المرأة التي نكحت بغير الإذن، فيجوز نكاحها بعد الثلاث عند الشافعي رحمه الله؛ لأن النكاح الأول لم ينعقد عنده كذا قيل قدماء أصحابه كالمزني والبويطي وأمثالهما. [الشافي: ص ٤٢] ما اختاره المتأخرون: فإنهم لم يجوزوا النكاح بعد الثلاث احتياطاً نظراً إلى اشتباه وقوعها على تقدير جواز هذا النكاح، والجوازه أيضاً وجوه لها قوة ما، وإن لم يجوزوه بها أيضاً احتياطاً في حل الفرج. وأما العام: اعلم أن حكم العام عند عامة الأشاعرة التوقف حتى يقوم دليل عموم وخصوص، وعند الثلجي والجبائي: الجزم بالخصوص كالواحد في الجنس والثلاثة في الجمع، والتوقف فيما فوق ذلك، وعند جمهور العلماء: إثبات الحكم فيما يتناوله من الأفراد قطعاً ويقيناً عند مشايخ العراق وعامة المتأخرين، وظناً عند جمهور الفقهاء والمتكلمين وهو مذهب الشافعي رحمه الله والمختار عند مشايخ سمرقند حتى يفيد وجوب العمل دون تخصيص العام من الكتاب بخبر الواحد والقياس هذا، ومتمسكات كل فريق في المطولات.
As for the general, then it is of two types: 1- general from which some individuals are excluded, 2- general from which nothing is excluded. So general means some of its individuals. Al-Hasan narrated from Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him): It is concluded with a suitable match, not otherwise. And similar is from Abu Yusuf (may Allah have mercy on him), and most of the mashayikh adopted this, and it is the chosen for fatwa. Malik and al-Shafi'i (may Allah have mercy on them) said: It is not concluded by their expressions. "Any woman, etc." is a hadith from 'Aisha, marfu'. At its end: "Her marriage is invalid, her marriage is invalid, her marriage is invalid. If he has consummated with her, then she deserves the dowry for what he has made lawful from her private parts. If they dispute, then the sultan is the guardian of the one who has no guardian." It was recorded by al-Shafi'i, Ahmad, Abu Dawud, al-Tirmidhi (and he declared it hasan), Ibn Majah, Abu 'Awanah, al-Tahawi, al-Hakim, and Ibn Hibban. And it has other aspects, and we also have aspects; if you wish to examine them, refer to the lengthy works. The repetition of "invalid" and the rest is to prevent figurative interpretation, meaning that what is meant by invalid is not incomplete, or it is due to the speaker's emphasis on the intended meaning. I say: The repetition three times, as understood from the expression of al-Khiyali, is in the context of rebuke and reprimand, as in his saying (peace be upon him): "Any slave who marries without the permission of his master, he is a fornicator, fornicator, fornicator" i.e., an adulterer, due to his disobedience to his master by marrying himself without his permission. Similarly, his saying (peace be upon him) regarding theft: "If he returns, then cut off his hand, cut off his hand." So his saying (peace be upon him): "Any woman, etc." is of this category. From it derives that marriage is concluded by the expression of women. And marriage: i.e., if the husband divorces this woman who married without permission three times, then it is permissible to marry her after three divorces according to al-Shafi'i (may Allah have mercy on him); because the first marriage was not concluded in his view, as said by his earlier companions like al-Muzani, al-Buwayti, and their peers. What the later ones chose: they did not permit marriage after three divorces as a precaution, considering the ambiguity of its occurrence on the assumption of permissibility of this marriage, and its permissibility also has aspects of some strength, even if they did not permit it also as a precaution regarding the lawfulness of the private part. As for the general: Know that the ruling concerning the general according to the majority of Ash'aris is suspension until evidence for generality and particularity comes. According to al-Thalji and al-Jubba'i: Certainty of particularity like the one in a species and the three in a plural, and suspension beyond that. According to the majority of scholars: Establishing the ruling regarding the individuals it encompasses with certainty and definitiveness according to the mashayikh of Iraq and the generality of later scholars, and with probability according to the majority of jurists and theologians, and this is the madhhab of al-Shafi'i (may Allah have mercy on him) and the chosen according to the mashayikh of Samarqand, so that it necessitates obligation to act without specifying the general from the Book by a khabar wahid and analogy. And the proofs of each group are in the lengthy works.
Source pages p. 15

Commentary
This passage defines 'amm (general) and classifies it into two types: one that has been specified (i.e., some individuals excluded) and one that has not been specified. The author then revisits the hadith about marriage without a guardian, explaining the repetition in the hadith as a rhetorical device for emphasis and rebuke, and notes that the Hanafi position is that a woman's nikah can be concluded by her own expression, contrary to Malik and Shafi'i. The passage then lists different epistemological views on 'amm: the Ash'aris suspend judgment until evidence for specification appears; some like al-Thalji and al-Jubba'i hold that small numbers are definite; the majority of scholars (including the Iraq Hanafis and later scholars) hold that 'amm is definitive (qat'i) in establishing the ruling for all individuals it covers, while the majority of jurists and theologians (including Shafi'i) consider it probable (zanni). The author states that the chosen view among the Samarqand mashayikh is that 'amm is definitive and can be acted upon without specification by a solitary hadith or analogy. This shows the Hanafi usul principle that general Quranic texts are not overridden by analogical reasoning.

Key Terms
عام (‘amm): A word that includes all individuals of its category without restriction.
تخصيص (takhsis): The exclusion of some individuals from the generality of a term.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school as stated in this passage, what is the epistemological status of a general (amm) text in the absence of a specifier?
A) Suspended until evidence appears.
B) Probable (zanni).
C) Definitive (qat'i) and must be acted upon.
D) It requires consensus to be binding.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school treats the general ('amm) as definitive (qat'i) until a specifier (mukhassis) is proven; this principle has direct impact on how general Quranic and hadith texts are applied.

The Ruling of 'Amm (General) and Its Application to the Thief's Liability
Defining 'amm and applying its ruling to a fiqh derivation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two types of 'amm, explain the Hanafi position that unspecified 'amm is definitive (qat'i), and apply it to derive the ruling on a thief's liability for destroyed stolen property.

Core Idea
Unspecified 'amm is definitive in the Hanafi school and cannot be abandoned by qiyas.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi classification of 'amm (general) into specified and unspecified types, and the critical difference between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools on the epistemological weight of general texts. We then see how this usul principle directly affects a fiqh ruling: whether a thief must compensate for stolen property that is destroyed after his hand is cut. By the end, you will be able to trace the derivation from the Quranic verse to the legal outcome.

Guided Path
1
Classify the types of 'amm
From the passage, identify that 'amm is divided into two types: general that has been specified (khuss) and general that has not been specified. The latter is the focus.
This classification is foundational to the discussion.
2
Identify the Hanafi ruling on unspecified 'amm
State that according to the Hanafi school (and the shaykhs of Iraq), unspecified 'amm is definitive (qat'i) in its indication and necessitates action on all its individuals with certainty.
Contrast with the Shafi'i view that it is presumptive (zanni).
3
Locate the dalil from the Quran
Find the verse 5:38 used in the passage: 'faqta'u aydiyahuma jaza'an bima kasaba.' Identify the operative word 'ma' that is claimed to be general.
The word 'ma' (ما) encompasses all acts of the thief.
4
Apply the principle to the thief case
Using the Hanafi rule that the general is definitive, argue that the cutting is the recompense for all that the thief has acquired (including destruction of the stolen property). If compensation were required, the cutting would only recompense some acts, thus abandoning part of the general. This is impermissible.
The analogy to usurpation (ghasb) proposed by al-Shafi'i is rejected because it would prioritize qiyas over the definitive text.
5
Note the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Hanafi – no compensation; Shafi'i – compensation required. This stems from the usul disagreement on the definitiveness of 'amm.
