The first research in the Book of Allah. Chapter on the Specific and the General. If evidence is established for specifying the remaining [of the general], it is permissible to specify it by a solitary report or by analogy until three remain, and after that it is not permissible. So it is obligatory to act upon it. And that is permissible only because the specifier that removed some from the whole, if it removed an unknown part, probability is established in every specific individual. So it is permissible that the individuals of the general are unspecified. Karkhi and Abu Abdullah al-Jurjani and others: that it does not remain a proof after specification, rather one must pause, whether the specified is known as in 'Kill the polytheists and do not kill the people of dhimmah' or unknown as if it were said: 'Kill the polytheists and do not kill some of them' except that it is necessary to specify the specification if known. And the majority said: if the specifier is unknown, the ruling of the generality falls so that it is no longer a proof in what remains, and one pauses for explanation; and if it is known, the general remains upon what it was in what lies beyond, by analogy with the exception of the unknown and the known. So in 'al-Fusul'. 'Its specification by a solitary report etc.': Example of specifying the general by a solitary report and analogy: Allah's saying 'So kill the polytheists' is a general text of zanni indication after its specification by the protected person, so it is specified by a solitary report, which is his saying (peace be upon him): 'Do not kill an old man, nor a woman, nor a child' just as it is specified also with respect to time by analogy on the protected person due to the cause of inability to fight, and so on until what remains of the general is an amount that the utterance of the general can be truthfully applied to, which is three in the plural, because the minimum of the plural is three. Specification is not allowed until three individuals remain, because it is only allowed by that by which abrogation is allowed, and the minimum of the plural is three by consensus of the scholars of language. If only one or two remain under the general, the general is no longer a reality but becomes abrogation and nullification, and abrogation of the general from the Book by a solitary report or analogy is not allowed. So in 'al-Fusul'. Because the specifier: from a verse or famous hadith or consensus. Its explanation: that the specified from the general, if it is an unknown part, like the prince saying: 'Kill the sons of so-and-so and do not kill some of them', every individual is probable to remain under the general and to be included under the evidence of specificity. When evidence is established that he is from the sum of those entered under the evidence of specificity, his specification side is given preponderance. And if it is a known part, then it is apparent that it is effectual by a cause, because the principle in texts is causation, and that cause is probable to exist in some of the remaining individuals, so probability is established in every specific individual. When evidence is established for the existence of that cause in this individual, his specification side is given preponderance. So it is established that the general includes probability in both cases, so its specification by solitary reports and analogy is allowed. So in 'al-Fusul'. 'An unknown part': like Allah's saying: 'And Allah has permitted trade and forbidden riba'. The verse 'And He has forbidden riba' is a specified unknown before the explanation by the six things, because riba in language is surplus, and surplus itself is not intended by consensus, because trade was only legislated for profit, so what is meant by riba is the legal riba and it was unknown. So in 'al-Ma'dan'. It remains under the ruling of the general, and it is possible to be included under the evidence of specificity, so the two aspects become equal, so it falls outside the ruling of the general in both entering and exiting with respect to the specific individual. When the legal evidence is established that it is from the sum of what entered under the evidence of specificity for that specific individual, his specification side is given preponderance. And if the specifier removed a known part from the whole, it remains outside its ruling in entering and exiting, it is possible that it is effectual by a cause present in this specific individual. When the legal evidence is established for the existence of that cause in other than this specific individual, the aspect of his specification is given preponderance, so it is acted upon with the existence of probability in the remaining.
Source pages p. 20

Commentary
This passage is a rule from Hanafi usul on the specification (takhsis) of a general term (amm) using zanni proofs like solitary reports (khabar al-wahid) and analogy (qiyas). The author follows the order: first, the general rule that specification is allowed as long as at least three individuals remain under the general; if fewer than three remain, it becomes abrogation (naskh), which is not allowed with zanni proofs. Second, the reasoning (ta'lil) behind this: when the specifier removes an unknown part, every individual in the general is equally probable to be intended or not, so zanni proofs can tilt the scale. When the specifier removes a known part, the cause (illa) of the ruling is assumed present in the remaining individuals, again allowing specification by zanni proofs. The passage also records a dispute: al-Karkhi, Abu Abdullah al-Jurjani, and others hold that after specification, the general ceases to be a proof (hujja) altogether and one must pause (tawaqquf). The majority (and the relied-upon Hanafi view) differentiate: if the specified part is unknown, the general loses its hujjiyya for the remaining until explanation; if known, the general remains a proof for what remains. The examples given include the famous hadith prohibiting killing women, children, and the elderly despite the general command to kill polytheists, and the riba verse which was unclear until the Prophet ﷺ specified it to six commodities. This lesson thus establishes the core Hanafi principle that general texts with zanni dalala can be specified by zanni proofs, preserving their authority for the remaining individuals.

Key Terms
تخصيص (takhsis): The specification of a general term by removing some of its individuals through evidence
خبر الواحد (khabar al-wahid): A solitary report that does not reach the level of tawatur; considered zanni in thubut
قياس (qiyas): Analogical deduction extending a ruling from an original case to a new case based on a shared cause (illa)
العام (al-amm): A term that encompasses all individuals of a category, like 'everyone' or 'all polytheists'

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority of Hanafi usul scholars, what is the minimum number of individuals that must remain under a general term after specification for the general to still be considered a valid general (amm)?
A) One individual
B) Two individuals
C) Three individuals
D) No minimum; even one is enough

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school allows specifying a general text by zanni proofs (khabar al-wahid, qiyas) provided at least three individuals remain under the general.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific

The Absolute of the Quran Cannot Be Qualified by Zanni Sources
States the Hanafi rule that mutlaq of Quran cannot be restricted by khabar al-wahid or qiyas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule that the absolute (mutlaq) of the Quran cannot be qualified by a khabar al-wahid or qiyas, apply it to the examples of wudu and hadd punishments, and evaluate the Shafi‘i counter-argument based on the distinction between bayan and naskh.

Core Idea
Adding a condition to a Quranic absolute changes the ruling — that is naskh, and a zanni source cannot abrogate a qat‘i text.

This lesson establishes a foundational Hanafi usul principle: the absolute commands of the Quran are definitive (qat‘i) and cannot be restricted or conditioned by speculative (zanni) sources like isolated hadith or analogy. We will explore the reasoning behind this rule, compare it with the Shafi‘i position, and see it applied to two key examples: the conditions for wudu and the punishment for zina.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rule and its rationale
Read the opening statement: 'It is not permissible (to qualify the absolute of the Book) by an isolated report or analogy.' Understand that the Hanafi argument rests on the difference in epistemological certainty—the Quran is qat‘i, while khabar al-wahid and qiyas are zanni. Adding a condition changes the ruling, constituting naskh (abrogation).
Naskh of a qat‘i text by a zanni source is invalid.
2
Analyze the naskh vs. bayan debate
Contrast the Hanafi position with Imam al-Shafi‘i's view. The Shafi‘i school sees such addition as bayan (clarification) rather than naskh. Hanafis respond that bayan requires prior ambiguity (ijmal), and the mutlaq is not ambiguous because it can be acted upon as is.
The key is whether the mutlaq is considered mujmal (ambiguous) or not.
3
Apply the rule to the wudu example
The verse 'Wash your faces' (5:6) commands absolute washing. The hadith 'Actions are but by intentions' cannot impose intention as a condition for validity. Instead, intention is sunnah, not fard. Similarly, order, continuity, and tasmiyah are not obligatory.
The text emphasizes that the absolute washing remains fard; extra conditions are sunnah.
4
Apply the rule to the zina example
The verse 'Flog each one of them one hundred lashes' (24:2) sets flogging as the absolute hadd. The hadith 'The virgin with the virgin: one hundred lashes and exile for a year' cannot add exile as part of the hadd. Exile is permissible as siyasah (policy), not as a fixed punishment.
The conjunction 'and' in the hadith is interpreted as permissive, not obligatory.
5
Summarize the thamarah al-khilaf
Identify the practical consequences: In wudu, Hanafis do not require intention, order, continuity, or tasmiyah for validity; Shafi‘is require some of these. In zina, Hanafis do not include exile in the hadd; Shafi‘is include it.
This shows how a usul principle directly shapes fiqh rulings.

Source Text

البحث الأول في كتاب الله
بخبر الواحد والقياس لا تجوز.
المطلق من الكتاب

فصل في المطلق والمقيد

مثاله: في قوله تعالى: ﴿فَاغْسِلُوا وُجُوهَكُمْ﴾، فالمأمور به هو الغَسْلُ على الإطلاق، فلا يزاد عليه شرط النية والترتيب والموالاة والتسمية بالخبر، ولكن يُعمل بالخبر على وجه لا يتغير به حكم الكتاب، فيقال: الغسلُ المطلق فرض بحكم الكتاب، والنية سنة بحكم الخبر.
بذلك الوجه المذكور بخبر الواحد إلخ لأن الإطلاق وصف مقصود في كلامهم، والزيادة عليه تكون نسخاً ورفعاً بوصف الإطلاق، فلا يجوز نسخ الكتاب أصله أو وصفه بخبر الواحد أو بالقياس؛ لأن الكتاب قطعي وخبر الواحد والقياس ظني خلافاً للشافعي له، فإنه يجوز الزيادة بخبر الواحد والقياس، ويجعل بياناً للمطلق من الكتاب؛ لأن المطلق يحتمل التقييد بالبيان، قلنا: إن البيان يقتضي سابقية الإجمال، ولا إجمال في المطلق لإمكان العمل به كذا في "الفصول". على الإطلاق: أي سواء كان النية أو بدونها، ومع الترتيب أو بدونه وكذا سائر السنن فلو شرط شيء من النية والترتيب ونحوهما للاختيار الواردة فيها لا يكون مطلق الغسل، ويكون نسخ إطلاق الكتاب بأخبار الآحاد، وذا لا يجوز كذا في "المعدن". شرط النية كما ذهب إليه الشافعي ومالك وأحمد وأبو ثور وداود له، لقوله عليه: "إنما الأعمال بالنيات" الحديث المشهور. [ حاشية الشيخ أكرم الندوي: ص ٢٨]
والترتيب كما هو مذهب الشافعي وأحمد وأبي عبيد لله، وسبب الاختلاف أمران: أحدهما: هل تفيد واو العطف في آية الوضوء الترتيب أم لا؟ والأمر الثاني: اختلافهم في أفعاله عليها هل هي محمولة على الوجوب أو على الندب؟ فإن النبي لا ل ا ل ل لم يتوضأ إلا مرتباً. [ حاشية الشيخ أكرم الندوي: ص ۲۸-۲۹] والموالاة: وهو قول مالك لله، لأن النبي واظب على الموالاة. [ حاشية الشيخ أكرم الندوي: ص ۲۹] والتسمية: وهو مذهب أصحاب الظواهر؛ لقوله عليها: "لا وضوء لمن لم يسم". [ حاشية الشيخ أكرم الندوي: ص ٢٩] بالخبر: وهو في النية قوله علي: "إنما الأعمال بالنيات، وإنما لامرء ما نوى، فمن كان هجرته إلى الله ورسوله فهجرته إلى الله ورسوله، ومن كانت هجرته إلى دنيا يصيبها أو امرأة ينكحها فهجرته إلى ما هاجر إليه" وفي الترتيب حديث: "هذا وضوء لا يقبل الله الصلاة إلا "به وكان مرتباً وفي المولاة حديث: "وأمره رجلاً صلى وفي قدمه لمعة بإعادة الوضوء والصلاة" رواه أبوداود، وفي التسمية حديث: "لا وضوء لمن لم يذكر اسم الله عليه" رواه أبو داود وأحمد وغيرهما كذا في شروح "الحسامي".

وكذلك قلنا في قوله تعالى: ﴿الزَّانِيَةُ وَالزَّانِي فَاجْلِدُوا كُلِّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا مِائَةَ جَلْدَةٍ﴾ إن الكتاب جعل جَلْدَ المائة حدًا للزنا، فلا يُزَادُ عليه التغريب حدا؛ لقوله عليه: "البكر بالبكر جلد مائة وتغريب عام" بل يُعمَل بالخبر على وجه لا يتغيَّرُ به حكم الكتاب، فيكون الجلد حدا شرعيًّا بحكم الكتاب والتغريب مشروعا سياسة بحكم الخبر. لكمال الزجر
وكذلك: أي مثل ما أجرينا الغسل والمسح على إطلاقها وتركنا الخبر بمقابلة مطلق الكتاب، قلنا في قوله تعالى: الزَّانِيَةُ وَالزَّانِي الآية. الزَّانِيَةُ وَالزَّانِي : أي غير المحصنة وغير المحصن؛ لأن حكمها ثابت بقوله تعالى: الشيخ والشيخة إذا زنيا فارجموهما نكالاً من الله، أو الحديث أو الإجماع، وإنما قدم الزانية على الزاني؛ لأن الزنا ينبعث عن الشهوة وهي في النساء أوفر، وقدم السارق على السارقة؛ لأن السرقة من الجرأة وهي في الرجال أكثر. حَدًا للزنا: لأنه مقرون بفاء الجزاء؛ إذ تقديره : الزانية والزاني إذا زنيا فاجلدوا وهو عقوبة زاجرة فكان حداً؛ لأن الحد هو العقوبة فإذا كان الجلد حداً وهو مطلق يقتضي أن يكون الجلد مجزياً في كونه زاجراً شرعاً سواء كان مع التغريب أو بدونه، فلو جعل التغريب حدا بالخبر لا يكون الجلد الخالي عن التغريب حدا؛ لأن الزاجر حينئذ هو المجموع، فلا يكون بعضه زاجراً، والحد هو الزاجر فإذا لم يكن الجلد حدا كان ذلك نسخاً للإطلاق كما مر في المثال السابق فافهم. البكر بالبكر إلخ أي عقوبة زناء البكر بالبكر أي الذكر الذي لم يتزوج بعد بالأنثى التي لم تزوج، والمراد بالبكر: غير المحصن، فالمحصن حده الرجم وقيد البكارة في كل منهما ليس احترازياً فلو أحدهما بكراً رجلاً أو امرأة، والآخر محصناً، فالبكر يجلد والمحصن يرجم. وتغريب عام أي سنة واحدة أي يجوز في عقوبة الجناية الأمران المذكوران أعني الجلد وتغريب عام، فعطف التغريب على الجلد يقتضي كون المجموع حدا، فلا يجوز الاكتفاء بأحدهما بنص القرآن يقتضي كفاية الجلد وحده، فصار هو جائزاً فرضاً وبقي التغريب جائزاً اصطلاحاً، وهو ما استوى فعله و تركه.
* أخرجه جه مسلم في "صحيحه" برقم: ١٦٩٠ ، باب حد الزنا، والترمذي رقم: ١٤٣٤، باب ما جاء في الرجم على الثيب، قال الترمذي: هذا حديث حسن صحيح، وأبو داود برقم ٤٤١٥ ، باب في الرجم، وابن ماجه، رقم: ٢٥٥٠، باب حد الزنا، والدارمي في باب في تفسير أَوْ يَجْعَلَ اللَّهُ لَهُنَّ سَبيلا الآية، والصحيح لابن حبان رقم: ٤٤٢٥ عن عبادة بن الصامت فيه.
The first research: Regarding the Book of Allah. It is not permissible (to qualify the absolute of the Book) by an isolated report or analogy. The absolute of the Book.

Chapter on the Absolute and the Qualified

Its example: In Allah's statement: "Wash your faces," the commanded act is washing absolutely, so the condition of intention, order, continuity, and saying Bismillah are not added by report, but the report is acted upon in a way that does not change the ruling of the Book. So it is said: The absolute washing is obligatory by the ruling of the Book, and intention is sunnah by the ruling of the report.

By that mentioned manner: with an isolated report etc., because absoluteness is an intended description in their speech, and adding to it would be abrogation and removal of the description of absoluteness. So it is not permissible to abrogate the essence or description of the Book by an isolated report or analogy, because the Book is definitive while isolated reports and analogy are speculative—contrary to al-Shafi‘i, may Allah have mercy on him, for he permits addition by isolated report and analogy, and considers it a clarification of the absolute of the Book, because the absolute can be qualified by clarification. We said: Clarification requires prior ambiguity, and there is no ambiguity in the absolute because it is possible to act upon it. So it is in al-Fusul. Absolutely: i.e., whether with intention or without it, and with order or without it, and similarly other sunan. If something of intention, order, and the like is stipulated, then it would not be absolute washing, and it would be abrogation of the absoluteness of the Book by isolated reports, and that is not permissible. So it is in al-Ma‘din. The condition of intention as held by al-Shafi‘i, Malik, Ahmad, Abu Thawr, and Dawud, due to his statement: "Actions are but by intentions" the famous hadith. [Footnote: p. 28]
And order as is the madhhab of al-Shafi‘i, Ahmad, and Abu ‘Ubayd, may Allah be pleased with them, and the reason for the disagreement are two matters: one: Does the coordinating waw in the verse of wudu indicate order or not? The second matter: Their disagreement concerning his actions, peace be upon him—are they taken as obligatory or recommendatory? For the Prophet, peace be upon him, did not perform wudu except in order. [Footnote: pp. 28-29] And continuity: which is the saying of Malik, may Allah be pleased with him, because the Prophet continuously performed wudu consecutively. [Footnote: p. 29] And saying Bismillah: which is the madhhab of the Zahiris, due to his statement: "No wudu for one who does not mention Allah's name." [Footnote: p. 29] By the report: and it is concerning intention: his statement: "Actions are but by intentions, and every man shall have what he intended. So whoever's emigration was for Allah and His Messenger, his emigration was for Allah and His Messenger, and whoever's emigration was for worldly gains or a woman to marry, his emigration was to what he emigrated for." And concerning order: the hadith: "This is the wudu without which Allah does not accept prayer" and it was ordered. And concerning continuity: the hadith: "He ordered a man who prayed with a dry spot on his foot to repeat the wudu and prayer" narrated by Abu Dawud. And concerning saying Bismillah: the hadith: "No wudu for one who does not mention the name of Allah over it" narrated by Abu Dawud, Ahmad, and others. So it is in the commentaries of al-Hisami.

And similarly we said regarding Allah's statement: "The female and male fornicator: flog each one of them one hundred lashes" that the Book made flogging one hundred lashes a fixed punishment for zina, so exile is not added to it as a hadd, due to his statement: "The virgin with the virgin: one hundred lashes and exile for a year." Rather, the report is acted upon in a way that does not change the ruling of the Book, so flogging is a legal hadd by the ruling of the Book, and exile is legislated as policy by the ruling of the report, for perfect deterrence.

And similarly: i.e., just as we applied washing and wiping absolutely and left the report in contrast to the absolute of the Book, we said regarding the verse: "The female and male fornicator" etc. "The female and male fornicator": i.e., the non-muhsan, because the ruling of the muhsan is established by His statement: "The old man and old woman, if they commit zina, stone them as a punishment from Allah," or by hadith or consensus. He mentioned the female fornicator before the male because zina is driven by desire and it is greater in women, and He mentioned the male thief before the female because theft is from audacity and it is greater in men. "One hundred lashes" as a hadd for zina: because it is coupled with the particle of result; its meaning: The female and male fornicator, if they commit zina, then flog them, and it is a deterrent punishment, so it is a hadd because the hadd is the punishment. So when flogging is a hadd and it is absolute, it necessitates that flogging alone is sufficient in being legally deterrent, whether with exile or without. If exile is made a hadd by report, then flogging without exile would not be a hadd, because the deterrent would then be the combination, so part of it would not be deterrent, and the hadd is the deterrent. So if flogging is not a hadd, that would be abrogation of the absoluteness, as in the previous example, so understand. "The virgin with the virgin" etc., i.e., the punishment of zina of a virgin with a virgin: the male who has not yet married and the female who has not married, and by 'virgin' is meant the non-muhsan. The muhsan's hadd is stoning. The restriction of virginity in each is not exclusory. If one of them is a virgin, male or female, and the other is muhsan, then the virgin is flogged and the muhsan is stoned. "And exile for a year": i.e., one year, meaning that both mentioned matters—flogging and exile for a year—are permissible in the punishment of the crime. The conjunction of exile to flogging implies that the combination is a hadd, so it is not permissible to be content with one of them, whereas the text of the Qur'an requires sufficiency of flogging alone. So flogging became permissible as an obligatory duty, and exile remained permissible as a convention, which is something whose doing and leaving are equal.
* Narrated by Muslim in his Sahih no. 1690, chapter on the hadd of zina; al-Tirmidhi no. 1434, chapter on stoning of the thayyib; al-Tirmidhi said: This hadith is hasan sahih; Abu Dawud no. 4415, chapter on stoning; Ibn Majah no. 2550, chapter on hadd of zina; al-Darimi in the chapter on interpretation of the verse "or Allah makes a way for them"; and Sahih of Ibn Hibban no. 4425 from ‘Ubadah ibn al-Samit.
Source pages p. 22

Commentary
This passage from Usul al-Shashi establishes a fundamental Hanafi usul rule: the absolute (mutlaq) of the Quran cannot be qualified (taqyid) or restricted by a khabar al-wahid (isolated report) or qiyas (analogy). The reason is that the Quranic text is qat‘i (definitive) in both its transmission and meaning, whereas khabar al-wahid and qiyas are zanni (speculative). Adding a condition to an absolute command from the Quran would change the ruling, which constitutes naskh (abrogation) — and abrogating a qat‘i text with a zanni one is impermissible. The author contrasts this with the position of Imam al-Shafi‘i, who permits such addition as bayan (clarification) rather than naskh, arguing that the absolute is ambiguous and can be clarified by the Sunnah. The Hanafi response is that the absolute is not ambiguous because it can be acted upon as is; thus, adding a condition is not clarification but abrogation. 

The text then applies this principle to two examples: (1) The absolute command in the wudu verse to wash the face cannot be qualified by conditions like intention, order, continuity, or saying Bismillah based on ahad reports. These are considered sunnah, not obligatory parts of the wudu. The Hanafis maintain that the fard is the absolute washing; the additional conditions from hadith are commendable but not required. (2) The absolute command to flog fornicators 100 lashes cannot be augmented by adding exile as a hadd punishment based on the hadith 'The virgin with the virgin: 100 lashes and exile for a year.' For the Hanafis, flogging remains the sole hadd; exile is permissible as a discretionary policy (siyasah), not as part of the fixed punishment. This preserves the Quranic text from being effectively abrogated by a zanni report. 

The passage also clarifies related points: the meaning of 'bikr' in the hadith is non-muhsan; if one party is muhsan, that person is stoned. The footnote provides the hadith sources. The marginal notes add references to the opinions of other madhhabs.

Key Terms
المطلق (al-mutlaq): An unqualified command in the Quran that can be acted upon as it is without any conditions or restrictions.
المقيد (al-muqayyad): A command that has been restricted by a condition, such as requiring intention in wudu.
خبر الواحد (khabar al-wahid): A report transmitted by one or a few narrators that does not reach the level of tawatur; zanni in transmission.
النسخ (al-naskh): Abrogation of a legal ruling by a later revelation or a stronger source; here, adding a condition to an absolute command is considered naskh because it changes the ruling.
البيان (al-bayan): Clarification of an ambiguous text; Shafi‘is view taqyid of mutlaq as bayan, not naskh.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, what is the status of the requirement of intention (niyyah) for wudu?
A) It is obligatory (fard) based on the hadith.
B) It is a condition for the validity of wudu.
C) It is sunnah, not part of the fard of washing.
D) It is prohibited because it adds to the Quran.

Key Takeaway
The absolute of the Quran is qat‘i and cannot be abrogated by zanni sources; added conditions become sunnah or siyasah, not part of the fard or hadd.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific

Al-Mushtarak and Al-Mu'awwal: Definition and Distinction
Defining mushtarak and mu'awwal and their relationship

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define al-mushtarak and al-mu'awwal, distinguish them from al-'amm, and apply the ta'wil process to determine the preferred meaning of a mushtarak word.

Core Idea
A word is mushtarak when placed for multiple meanings; after interpretation (ta'wil), it becomes mu'awwal with one preferred meaning.

In this lesson, we explore two foundational concepts of Hanafi usul al-fiqh: al-mushtarak (the common term) and al-mu'awwal (the interpreted term). Understanding these terms is crucial for correctly interpreting ambiguous texts in the Quran and Hadith. The passage defines mushtarak as a word placed for two different meanings and explains that mu'awwal is the same word after a preferred meaning has been chosen through ta'wil, a form of ijtihad. This distinction helps us see how the same word can carry different legal implications depending on context and evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Core Definition of Mushtarak
Locate the phrase 'المشترك: ما وُضِع لمعنيين مختلفين' and note that mushtarak is defined as a word placed for two (or more) different meanings. This placement is repeated, each for a separate meaning.
The definition is axiomatic for the rest of the discussion.
2
Distinguish Mushtarak from 'Amm
Read the commentary that contrasts 'amm and mushtarak. 'Amm indicates all individuals of a single meaning by one placement; mushtarak indicates multiple meanings by separate placements on the basis of interchange. Understand that 'amm is general in one sense, while mushtarak is ambiguous between different senses.
This distinction prevents confusion between two types of general words.
3
Understand Mu'awwal as the Interpreted Mushtarak
Note that mu'awwal is defined as a mushtarak turned towards one of its meanings through ta'wil (preponderance). Recognize that before preference, the word is mushtarak; after preference, it becomes mu'awwal. They are two states of the same word.
Ta'wil is a legitimate ijtihad tool in Hanafi usul.
4
Recognize the Broader Hanafi Definition
The passage notes that the usuli's mushtarak includes cases where the multiple meanings arise from multiple placements, or from a single concept that cannot be simultaneously intended, or even from a single meaning with two probable interpretations (like kinayat in divorce). This is broader than the linguist's definition which requires multiple original placements.
This expansion affects how we classify words in legal texts.

Source Text

فصل في المشترك والمؤول
المشترك: ما وُضِع لمعنيين مختلفين، لفظ
وقال البعض: هذا جواب آخر للنقض الثاني أي قال بعض أصحابنا وهو مذهب الجمهور: قيد الدخول يثبت بالخبر وهو من المشاهير فحينئذ لا يلزم تقييد الكتاب بخبر الواحد بل بالخبر المشهور.
المشترك إلخ: الفرق بين العام والمشترك: أن العام يدل على جميع ما يشتمل عليه اللفظ بوضع واحد، وفي حالة واحدة، والمشترك يدل على أكثر من معنى واحد بأوضاع مختلفة على سبيل التبادل. [حاشية الشيخ أكرم الندوي: ٣٦] المؤول قسم من المشترك بحسب الظاهر؛ إذ هو المشترك المصروف إلى أحد معانيه المرجح إرادته بنحو

من التأويل، وضرب من الاجتهاد ولعل :التحقيق أنه قسيم له، والفرق في جلي النظر بحسب الاعتبار، الواحد قبل الترجح مشترك وبعده مؤول، أو من حيث الاشتراك وتساويها وضعاً مشترك، ومن حيث صرفه وتأويله إلى أحدها مؤول، فيجتمعان في زمان أيضاً كما اجتمعا على الأول في لفظ ومحل واحد، وفي دقيق النظر بحسب الذات؛ إذ المشترك أمر كلي ومفهوم عام يعرض الألفاظ الخاصة وكذا المؤول، وهذان المفهومان متبائنان طبعاً وحقيقة؛ إذ طبيعة أحدهما مغايرة بالذات للطبيعة الآخر وإن لم يكونا متبائنين بالذات كالعرضيات مع المعروضات، أو مع العرضيات الأخر كالضاحك والكاتب والإنسان، ثم تعريفه بما وضع إلخ ليس على ظاهره، بل مراده ما أطلق أو استعمل في عرف به التخاطب في معنيين مختلفين أي مرادين منه سواء كان اختلافهما ناشياً من تعدد وضعه، أو كان متحدين في مفهوم هو الموضوع له مختلفين في عدم اجتماعهما في الإرادة، أو كانا مختلفين باختلاف الاحتمالين في مدلوله المقصود منه وإن كان معناه واحد كما في كنايات الطلاق بائن وبتة، ومن ههنا يظهر أنه ليس مشترك الأصولي ما هو المشهور في العرف واللغة والصناعات الآخر المعتبر فيه تعدد الوضع الأصلي، وقد يستبين هذا من الأمثلة الآتية أيضاً كذا في "الحصول". ما وُضع إلخ: أي وضعاً مكرراً مرة لمعنى
Chapter on the Common (Mushtarak) and the Interpreted (Mu'awwal). Al-Mushtarak: a word placed for two different meanings. And some said: This is another answer to the second objection, i.e., some of our companions (the school of the majority) said: The condition of consummation is established by the hadith, and it is among the famous (reports), so then they are not obliged to restrict the Book with a solitary hadith, but with a famous hadith. Al-Mushtarak, etc.: The difference between al-‘Amm and al-Mushtarak: that al-‘Amm indicates all that the word encompasses by a single placement and in one state, while al-Mushtarak indicates more than one meaning by different placements on a basis of interchange. [Hashiyat al-Shaykh Akram al-Nadawi: 36] Al-Mu'awwal is a division of al-Mushtarak in appearance, because it is al-Mushtarak turned towards one of its meanings with preponderance indicating intent by way of interpretation (ta'wil), which is a type of ijtihad. Perhaps the verification is that it is its counterpart. The difference in clear consideration according to viewpoint: the same word before preponderance is mushtarak, after it is mu'awwal; or from the perspective of sharing and equality in placement it is mushtarak, and from the perspective of turning and interpreting it to one of them it is mu'awwal. So they also combine in time, just as they combined in the first view in one word and one place. In subtle consideration according to essence: because mushtarak is a universal matter and a general concept that occurs to specific words, and likewise mu'awwal. These two concepts are naturally and genuinely distinct, because the nature of one is essentially different from the nature of the other, even if they are not essentially distinct like accidents with substances, or with other accidents like 'laughing' and 'writer' and 'human'. Then its definition including 'placed for' etc. is not literal; rather what is intended is 'what is used or employed in the convention of discourse with two different meanings' i.e., intended from it, whether the difference arises from multiple placements, or they are united in concept as the placed-for but differ in not being combined in intent, or they differ by difference of probability in its intended meaning even if its meaning is one, as in kinayat of divorce 'ba'in' and 'batta'. From here it becomes apparent that the mushtarak of the usuli is not what is famous in custom, language, and other arts where multiple original placements are considered. This may become clear from the following examples as well, as in al-Husul. 'Placed for' means placed repeatedly once for a meaning.
Source pages p. 28

Commentary
This passage defines 'mushtarak' (common term) and 'mu'awwal' (interpreted term) in Hanafi usul. The opening line gives the classic definition: mushtarak is a word placed for two different meanings. A brief note interjects a different answer to a previous objection about consummation, attributing it to 'some of our companions' referring to the famous hadith (not solitary). Then a detailed commentary explains the difference between 'amm and mushtarak: 'amm indicates all its individuals by one placement, while mushtarak indicates multiple meanings by separate placements on the basis of interchange. The term 'mu'awwal' is initially presented as a subdivision of mushtarak (in appearance), as it is the same word after preferring one meaning over others through ta'wil (interpretation). However, the commentary suggests that in reality, mushtarak and mu'awwal are distinct concepts: before preference, the word is mushtarak; after preference, it becomes mu'awwal. Additionally, from an essential perspective, they are different universals that apply to particular words. The definition 'placed for' is not literal; it refers to usage in discourse for two different intended meanings. This can arise from multiple original placements, or from a single concept that cannot be simultaneously intended, or from a word with a single meaning that has two probable interpretations (like kinayat of divorce). The usuli's mushtarak differs from the common linguist's mushtarak, which requires multiple original placements. Examples are promised later.

Key Terms
المشترك (al-mushtarak): A word placed for two or more different meanings, used in discourse where each meaning is intended separately.
المؤول (al-mu'awwal): A mushtarak term after preferring one of its meanings through interpretation (ta'wil) based on evidence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the difference between al-‘amm and al-mushtarak?
A) ‘Amm indicates all individuals by one placement; mushtarak indicates multiple meanings by separate placements.
B) ‘Amm can be restricted; mushtarak cannot.
C) Mushtarak is a type of ‘amm.
D) There is no difference; they are synonymous.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, a word is mushtarak when it carries multiple intended meanings; through ta'wil (interpretation) it becomes mu'awwal, a distinct conceptual state with a preferred meaning.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific

Definition and Ruling of al-Mushtarak (Common Term)
Defines mushtarak and mu'awwal with examples and ruling.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define al-mushtarak and al-mu'awwal, and apply their ruling when interpreting a text.

Core Idea
A mushtarak word has multiple meanings, but once one is intended, the others are disregarded — interpretation is required.

In this lesson, we examine the concept of al-mushtarak (the common term) from Usul al-Shashi. Mushtarak words are single words that have been placed for multiple distinct meanings. Understanding how to treat such words is crucial in Hanafi usul, as it affects how we interpret ambiguous terms in the Qur'an and Sunnah. The passage also introduces al-mu'awwal — the interpreted version of a mushtarak.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition of al-mushtarak
A single word placed for two or more different meanings through separate coinages.
The word must be placed for each meaning independently, not as a collective whole.
2
List the examples from the passage
Jāriya (female slave / ship), mushtarī (buyer / star), bā'in (separation / clarity).
These illustrate how context determines intended meaning.
3
State the ruling (hukm) of mushtarak
When one meaning is determined as intended, consideration of the other meaning falls away.
Simultaneous intention of multiple meanings is not permissible.
4
Define al-mu'awwal
The mushtarak turned towards one of its meanings by preponderance through evidence (ta'wīl).
Mu'awwal is the post-interpretation state of a mushtarak.

فصل في المشترك والمؤول
المشترك: ما وضع لمعنيين مختلفين، لفظ واحد. مثاله: جارية للأمة والسفينة، والمشتري لقابل عقد البيع وكوكب السماء، والبائن للبين والبيان. وحكم المشترك: أنه إذا تعين الوحد مراداً به سقط اعتبار إرادة غيره. والمؤول: هو المشترك المصروف إلى أحد معانيه المرجح إرادته بنحو التأويل.
Section on the Common and the Interpreted. The common: a single word placed for two different meanings. Example: 'jāriya' for female slave and ship; 'mushtarī' for the acceptor of a sale contract and a star in the sky; 'bā'in' for separation and clarity. The ruling of the common: when one [meaning] is determined as intended, consideration of intending the other falls away. The interpreted: the common turned towards one of its meanings whose intention is preponderant by means of interpretation.
Source pages p. 28

Commentary
This passage from Usul al-Shashi defines two key terms: al-mushtarak (the common term) and al-mu'awwal (the interpreted term). The author begins by stating that a mushtarak is a single word that has been placed (wad') for two or more different meanings. This placement is repeated—once for each meaning—either due to forgetfulness of the first coiner or to separate coinages. Importantly, the word is not placed for the collective whole at once; that would be impossible. Examples given: 'jāriya' can mean a female slave or a ship; 'mushtarī' can mean the buyer in a contract or a celestial body; 'bā'in' can mean separation (as in divorce) or clarity. The ruling (hukm) of such a term is that if one specific meaning is clearly intended by the speaker, then the possibility of intending the other meaning is disregarded. This is because intending multiple distinct meanings simultaneously in a single utterance is not permissible in the Hanafi usul view—the mind can only attend to one meaning at a time. Then the passage briefly defines 'al-mu'awwal': it is the mushtarak that is turned or directed towards one of its meanings, and that meaning is considered preponderant (rājiḥ) through some evidence or context (ta'wīl). Thus, mu'awwal is essentially the mushtarak after it has been interpreted. This distinction is crucial in Hanafi usul for understanding how ambiguous terms in the Qur'an and Sunnah are resolved.

Key Terms
المشترك (al-mushtarak): A single word placed (wad‘) for two or more different meanings through repeated coinage.
المؤول (al-mu'awwal): The mushtarak after it has been turned towards one of its meanings by preponderance (tarjīḥ) through evidence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling (hukm) of a mushtarak term when one of its meanings is clearly intended?
A) All meanings are considered equally valid.
B) The intended meaning is accepted and the other meaning is dropped from consideration.
C) The word becomes majāz for the non-intended meanings.
D) The word is considered mu'awwal without any need for evidence.

Key Takeaway
A mushtarak term has multiple meanings, but only one is intended; the others are disregarded once one is determined.

The Principle of Mushtarak: No Generality
Defines mushtarak and applies to jaza' al-sayd

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why mushtarak has no general coverage (la 'umum) and apply this principle to derive the Hanafi ruling on the penalty for hunting.

Core Idea
A word shared between meanings cannot indicate all at once; the intended meaning must be preponderated by context.

This lesson introduces the first of two foundational concepts: al-mushtarak (the homonym). The passage from Usul al-Shashi demonstrates how the lack of generality in mushtarak leads to a specific fiqhi ruling on the penalty for a muhrim who kills game. We will unpack the linguistic principle and see how it resolves an apparent ambiguity in the Quran.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Quranic text and the disputed word
Locate the verse (al-Ma'idah 5:95) and the word 'mithl'. Determine that it is mushtarak between likeness in form and likeness in value.
The word 'mithl' has two distinct meanings.
2
Define mushtarak and its legal property
Understand the definition of mushtarak as a word with multiple distinct meanings. The Hanafi principle: no generality (la 'umum) for mushtarak – it cannot indicate all meanings simultaneously.
This is key to the Hanafi position.
3
Apply the principle to the penalty case
Since combining form and value is impossible (istihalah al-jam'), the form must be dropped. The preponderant meaning (value) is taken, yielding the ruling: compensation by value, not by a physical counterpart.
This is the mufta bihi view of Abu Hanifa.
4
Analyze the inter-madhhab dispute
Compare with the positions of al-Shafi'i, Malik, Ahmad, and Muhammad ibn al-Hasan who require physical likeness for animals with a counterpart. Identify their dalil (literal meaning) and the Hanafi response (mushtarak cannot be general).
The thamarah al-khilaf: a muhrim killing a deer – Hanafi pays value, Shafi'i sacrifices a sheep.
5
Conclude with the operative ruling
State the mufta bihi: the penalty is the value of the game, with options for food or fasting as detailed in the text.

Source Text

البحث الأول في كتاب الله فصل في المشترك والمؤول وعلى هذا قلنا: لا يجب النظير في جزاء الصيد؛ لقوله تعالى: فَجَزَاء مِثْلُ مَا قَتَلَ مِنَ النعمه الآية؛ لأن المثل مشترك بين المثل صورة، وبين المثل معنى وهو القيمة، وقد أُريد في الجسم من حيث المالية المثلُ من حيث المعنى بهذا النص في قتل الحمام والعُصْفُور ونحوهما بالاتفاق، فلا يراد المثلُ وهو القيمة المذكور من حيث الصورة؛ إذ لا عموم للمشتَرَك أصلاً، فَيَسْقُطُ اعتبار الصورة لاستحالة الجمع. لا حقيقة ولا مجازا ثم إذا ترجّح بعضُ وجوه المشترك بغالب الرأي يصير مؤوَّلاً. في المثل لا يجب النظير إلخ أي خلقة، وقد قال بوجوبه الشافعي ومالك وأحمد وغيرهم له، ومحمد بن الحسن له من أصحابنا حيث قالوا: يجب النظير فيما له نظير في الخلقة، ففي الظبي الشاة، وفي الأرنب عناق، وعند إمامنا الأعظم له: يجب المثل معنى وهي القيمة، وبيانه إذا قتل المحرم صيداً فجزاؤه أن يقوم الصيد في المكان الذي قتل فيه، أو في أقرب المواضع إذا كان في بر فيقومه ذوا عدل ثم هو يخير، إن شاء ابتاع بها هدياً وذبحه إن بلغت هدياً، وإن شاء اشترى بها طعاماً ويتصدق على كل مسكين نصف صاع من بر، أو صاعاً من تمر أو شعير، وإن شاء صام على ما ذكر في موضعه. لا عموم للمشتَرَك : المراد بعموم المشترك: أن يشمل جميع معانيه، وهذا منعه الحنفية وجمهور الأصوليين وجميع أهل اللغة، وبعض المحققين من أصحاب الشافعي، وقال الشافعية وبعض الأصوليين: إن الأصل هو أن المشترك لا يدل إلا على معنى واحد ولكن يجوز أن يطلق على كل معانيه بطريق الحقيقة إذا صح الجمع بينهما . [ حاشية الشيخ أكرم الندوي: ص ٣٨] بغالب الرأي: أي الظن الحاصل بالقياس أو خبر الواحد أو القرائن الأخرى في النصوص، وأما مثال النقود في الحكميات فمبني على ما عرفت من أن المشترك لا يجب تعدد الوضع بل يكفيه تعدد المختلفات أيضاً ولو في معنى واحد من جهة اختلاف المصاديق أو تكثر الموارد أو غيرهما، والمراد بغالب نقد البلد أي بلد البائع لا المتبايعين: ما هو الأروج فيه والأرجح على غيره من الأثمان بالتعارف ومزيد الاستعمال وهو إحدى قرائن الإرادة وأمارتها، فيكون كالقياس والخبر في إيراث الظن، وقوله مختلفة أي مختلفة المالية، والمراد به: أن يكون الكل سواء في الرواج كذا في "الهداية". يصير مؤوَّلاً إلخ: المؤول مأخوذ من آل يؤل إذا رجع وأولته إذا رجعته وصرفته؛ لأنك متى تأملت في اللفظ وصرفته عما يحتمل من الوجوه المحتملة إلى وجه فقد رجعته إليه والمراد به ههنا هو المؤول من المشترك لا وحكم المؤَوَّل وجوبُ العَمْل به مع احتمال الخطأ. وذلك ومثاله: في الحكميَّات ما قلنا: إذا أطلق الثمن في البيع كان على غالب نقد البلد، تعيين غالب نقد البلد بطريق التأويل، ولو كانت النقود مختلفة فسد البيع؛ لما ذكرنا. وحمل الأقراء على في البلد بأن بين القدر دون الصفة من استحالة الجمع وعدم الرجحان الحيض، وحملُ النكاح في الآية على الوطء، وحمل الكنايات حال مذاكرة الطلاق على الطلاق من المشترك بين العقد والوطء عن الطلاق مذا القبيل، وعلى هذا قلنا: الدَّينُ المانع من الزكاة يصرف إلى أيسر أي التأويل المالين قضاء للدين. وفرَّع محمد محله على هذا فقال: "إذا تزوج امرأة على نصاب، وله نصاب من الغنم، ميهم من نصاب الزكاة المؤول مطلقاً فافهم مع احتمال الخطأ أما في تأويله؛ لأن التأويل لا يكون إلا بأمر ظني، وهو يستلزم احتمال الغلط؛ لأن المجتهد يخطئ ويصيب، وفي بعض النسخ لفظه "على" بدل "مع" لكن يكون "على" حينئذ بمعنى "مع" كما يقال : فلان بحر في العلوم على صغر سنه أي مع صغر سنه. بر سر بالله فسد البيع إلخ لاستحالة الجمع وعدم الرجحان إلا إذا بين أحدهما فحينئذ ترتفع الجهالة المفضية إلى النزاع، والفساد إنما كان لأجلها وحمل الأقراء أي في آية التربص وهو قوله تعالى: ﴿وَالْمُطَلَّقَاتُ يَتَرَبَّصْنَ بِأَنْفُسِهِنَّ ثَلاثَةَ قُرُوع الآية. [الشافي: ص ٦٣] وحمل الكنايات: أي في قول الرجل لزوجته: أنت بائن. [الشافي: ص ٦٣] من هذا القبيل أي من قبيل التأويل؛ وذلك لأن القروء مشترك بين الحيض والطهر والنكاح مشترك بين الوطء والعقد، وألفاظ الكنايات كالبائن مثلاً مشترك يحتمل أن يكون من البيان أو من البين، فإذا حمل القروء على الحيض والنكاح على الوطء وكنايات الطلاق حال مذاكرة الطلاق على أن المراد بها الانقطاع من وصلة النكاح كان ذلك تأويلاً كذا في "الشروح". وعلى هذا: أي أن المحتمل للشيئين يصرف إلى أحد محتمليه بدليل يفيد غلبة الظن كما في الألفاظ المشتركة. إلى أيسر المالين: أي إذا كان لرجل نصب من الدراهم والدنانير والعروض والسوائم، وعليه دين يستغرق بعضه، يصرف أولاً إلى النقود؛ لأن قضاء الدين منه أيسر ; لعدم الاحتياج فيه إلى البيع، ثم إلى العروض؛ لأنها عرضة، ثم إلى السوائم؛ لأنها فاضلة عن الحاجة، ثم إلى المشغول بحاجة كدار السكنى وثياب البدن، ودواب الركوب، وعبيد الخدمة وغيرها.
The first research on the Book of Allah. Chapter on the Common (Mushtarak) and the Interpreted (Mu'awwal). And upon this we said: The likeness (al-nazir) is not obligatory in the penalty for hunting, due to the statement of Allah Most High: 'So the penalty is a like (mithl) of what he has killed from the cattle' the verse; because mithl is common (mushtarak) between likeness in form and likeness in meaning which is value, and it has been intended by this text in the body regarding wealth the likeness in meaning, in killing a pigeon, sparrow, and the like by agreement, so the likeness mentioned (which is value) is not intended in terms of form, because there is no generality for the common term (mushtarak) at all, so consideration of form drops due to impossibility of combination. Neither as a reality nor as a metaphor. Then if some aspects of the common term become preponderant by predominant opinion, it becomes interpreted (mu'awwal). Regarding mithl: 'the likeness is not obligatory' etc., meaning physical form; and al-Shafi'i, Malik, Ahmad and others held its obligation, and Muhammad ibn al-Hasan among our companions also held it, as they said: the physical likeness is obligatory for what has a physical likeness; for a gazelle, a sheep; for a rabbit, a young goat; and according to our great Imam (Abu Hanifa), the likeness in meaning is obligatory, i.e., its value. Its explanation: when a muhrim kills game, his penalty is to appraise the game in the place where it was killed, or in the nearest place if it was in a desert; two just persons appraise it; then he has a choice: if he wishes, he purchases a sacrificial animal with that amount and slaughters it if it reaches the value of a sacrificial animal; if he wishes, he purchases food and gives in charity to each poor person half a sa' of wheat or one sa' of dates or barley; if he wishes, he fasts as mentioned in its place. 'No generality for the common term': the meaning of generality of the common term (mushtarak) is that it includes all its meanings; and this is denied by the Hanafis, the majority of usulists, and all linguists, and some researchers among the followers of al-Shafi'i; and the Shafi'is and some usulists said: the principle is that the common term (mushtarak) does not indicate except one meaning, but it is permissible to use it for all its meanings by way of reality if combination between them is possible. [Hashiyat al-Shaykh Akram al-Nadwi: p. 38] 'By predominant opinion': i.e., the zann (conjecture) obtained by qiyas, khabar al-wahid, or other contexts in the texts. As for the example of currencies in legal matters, it is based on what you have known that mushtarak does not require multiplicity of wad' (linguistic assignment), but rather multiplicity of different things is sufficient for it, even in one meaning from the perspective of difference of applications or multiplicity of instances or other aspects. The intended meaning of 'the predominant currency of the country' is that of the country of the seller, not of the two contractors: whatever is the most circulated and preponderant over other prices by custom and extensive use, which is one of the contexts of intention and its indicators, so it is like qiyas and khabar in producing zann. And his statement 'different' means different in value, and the intent is that all are equal in circulation, as in al-Hidayah. 'It becomes mu'awwal' etc.: mu'awwal is derived from aala ya'ulu if it returns, and awwaltuhu if I returned it and diverted it; because when you reflect on the word and divert it from the possible aspects to one aspect, you have returned it to it, and the intended meaning here is the mu'awwal from the common term (mushtarak), not... The ruling of the mu'awwal is the obligation of acting upon it with the possibility of error. And that is so. And its example in legal matters is what we said: when the price is mentioned absolutely in a sale, it is upon the predominant currency of the country; specifying the predominant currency of the country is by way of interpretation (ta'wil). If the currencies were different, the sale becomes invalid due to what we mentioned. And the interpretation of 'quru' in the verse as menstruation, and the interpretation of 'nikah' in the verse as intercourse, and the interpretation of kinayat (allusions) during the discussion of divorce as divorce, from what is common between marriage and intercourse, about divorce of this category. And upon this we said: the debt that prevents zakat is paid from the easiest of the two assets as a means of fulfilling the debt. And Muhammad derived a branch upon this and said: 'If a man marries a woman on a nisab, and he has a nisab of sheep, it is from the nisab of zakat, the mu'awwal absolutely, so understand.' With the possibility of error regarding his interpretation; because interpretation (ta'wil) is only by a zanni matter, which entails the possibility of error because the mujtahid errs and hits. In some copies, the word 'ala is used instead of ma'a, but then 'ala in this context means ma'a, as it is said: 'He is a sea of knowledge 'ala (despite) his young age,' i.e., ma'a (with) his young age. 'The sale becomes invalid' etc., due to impossibility of combination and lack of preponderance unless one of them is specified, then the ambiguity leading to dispute is removed; invalidity is due to it. And the interpretation of 'quru' is in the verse of waiting period, which is His statement: 'And divorced women shall wait for three quru' the verse. [al-Shafi: p. 63] And the interpretation of kinayat: i.e., the saying of a man to his wife: 'You are ba'in' [al-Shafi: p. 63] is from this category, i.e., from the category of interpretation; because quru' is common between menstruation and purity, and nikah is common between intercourse and marriage, and the words of kinayat like 'ba'in' for example are common, possibly meaning separation or distance. So when quru' is interpreted as menstruation, and nikah as intercourse, and kinayat of divorce during discussion of divorce as intended for separation from the marriage bond, that is interpretation (ta'wil), as in the commentaries. 'And upon this': meaning that what is possible for two things is diverted to one of its possibilities by a proof that yields predominant conjecture (ghalabat al-zann), as in common words. 'To the easiest of the two assets': i.e., if a man has dinars, dirhams, goods, and grazing animals, and he owes a debt that consumes some of them, he first pays from cash, because paying the debt from it is easier due to no need for sale; then from goods because they are at hand; then from grazing animals because they are surplus to need; then from items occupied by need such as a residential house, body garments, riding animals, and service slaves, and other things.
Source pages p. 31

Commentary
This passage from Usul al-Shashi is a foundational exposition of two critical concepts in Hanafi usul al-fiqh: al-mushtarak (the homonym) and al-mu'awwal (the interpreted meaning). The author opens with a fiqhi application: the penalty for a muhrim (person in ihram) who kills game. The Quranic verse (al-Ma'idah 5:95) says 'fa-jaza'un mithlu ma qatala min an-na'am.' The word 'mithl' is mushtarak—it can mean similarity in form or similarity in value. The Hanafi position, following Imam Abu Hanifa, holds that it means value, not a physical likeness. This is because mushtarak has no general coverage (la 'umum lil-mushtarak), meaning it cannot simultaneously refer to all its possible meanings. Since combining both form and value is impossible, the form is dropped and value is deemed intended by preponderance of evidence (ghalabat al-dhann). The passage then notes the ikhtilaf: Shafi'i, Malik, Ahmad, and even Muhammad ibn al-Hasan among the Hanafis hold that the physical likeness is obligatory for animals that have a physical counterpart (e.g., a sheep for a gazelle). But the relied-upon Hanafi position is value, with detailed rules for substitution by food or fasting. The text then defines mushtarak and the principle that it cannot be used for all meanings simultaneously except by way of metaphor (majaz), though some Shafi'is allow it if combination is possible. The concept of mu'awwal is introduced: when one meaning of a mushtarak becomes preponderant due to a contextual indicator (qarīna), the word becomes 'interpreted' and must be acted upon, even though there remains a possibility of error. Examples include: interpreting the price in a sale by the predominant currency of the country; interpreting 'quru'' in the verse on 'iddah as menstruation (Hanafi view, as opposed to Shafi'i who interpret as purity); interpreting 'nikah' in a certain verse as intercourse; and interpreting kinayat (allusions) during discussions of divorce as actual divorce. Another application: a debt that prevents zakat should be paid from the most readily available assets (e.g., cash before goods). Muhammad al-Shaybani derives a branch ruling: if a man marries a woman for a specific nisab and he has a nisab of sheep, that falls under the mu'awwal as well. The commentary emphasizes that all these rulings are based on the usul principle that mushtarak is not general and that interpretation (ta'wil) is based on predominant zann (conjecture), which inherently carries the possibility of error—hence the mujtahid may be wrong. The passage concludes with practical details of how to determine the easiest asset for debt repayment. Throughout, the author maintains a consistent Hanafi usul framework, distinguishing it from the Shafi'i school on the nature of mushtarak and the method of interpretation.

Key Terms
المشترك (al-mushtarak): A word that has multiple distinct meanings by linguistic usage, e.g., 'ayn (eye, spring, gold coin). It has no general coverage (la 'umum) and indicates only one meaning at a time, determined by context.
المثل (al-mithl): In the verse, it is mushtarak between likeness in form (physical similarity) and likeness in value (monetary equivalent). The Hanafi position chooses value.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi usul position in this passage, why is a muhrim who kills a pigeon not required to offer a physically similar pigeon as a penalty?
A) Because pigeons have no physical counterpart in the animal kingdom.
B) Because the word 'mithl' in the verse is mushtarak and cannot indicate both form and value, and combining them is impossible, so the preponderant meaning (value) is taken.
C) Because the Prophet (ﷺ) specifically allowed money payments for small game.
D) Because the Hanafi school always prefers monetary compensation over physical sacrifice.

Key Takeaway
Mushtarak has no general coverage; the intended meaning is determined by preponderance of contextual evidence.

Mu'awwal: Acting on Preponderant Meaning
Defines mu'awwal and lists fiqhi examples

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define mu'awwal, identify examples from the text, and apply the principle that mu'awwal is acted upon despite possibility of error.

Core Idea
When a mushtarak word's meaning is preponderated by context, it becomes mu'awwal and must be acted upon, even though error remains possible.

Having understood that mushtarak has no generality, we now explore what happens when one meaning becomes preponderant: the word becomes 'mu'awwal' (interpreted). This lesson examines the definition of mu'awwal, its ruling (obligation to act), and several practical examples from the text: determining the predominant currency in a sale, interpreting 'quru'' as menstruation, and prioritizing assets for debt repayment.

Guided Path
1
Define mu'awwal and its ruling
Understand that mu'awwal is the mushtarak after preponderance (tarjih) of one meaning by a contextual indicator. Its ruling: wajib al-'amal bihi (obligation to act upon it), though it retains the possibility of error (ihtimal al-khata').
This is derived from the root aala – to return; the word is 'returned' to one meaning.
2
Understand the scope of mu'awwal in legal matters
The text gives several fiqhi examples: (a) absolute mention of price in a sale refers to the predominant currency of the seller's country; (b) quru' in the iddah verse is interpreted as menstruation; (c) nikah in a certain verse as intercourse; (d) kinayat (allusions) during divorce discussions as actual divorce.
Each illustrates how context determines preponderance.
3
Analyze the example of currency and debt
When the price is mentioned absolutely in a sale, it is interpreted as the predominant currency of the country. If currencies are different without specification, the sale is invalid (fasid) due to ambiguity. For debt repayment, the easiest asset (usually cash) is prioritized.
This shows the practical impact of ta'wil in mu'amalat.
4
Trace the derivation of a branch ruling by Muhammad al-Shaybani
Muhammad derives: if a man marries a woman on a specific nisab (e.g., a debt), and he has another nisab of sheep, the debt is considered mu'awwal; the ruling follows the preponderant interpretation.
This illustrates ijtihad within the school.
5
Conclude with the epistemological status of mu'awwal
Ta'wil is based on zann (predominant conjecture), not certainty. The mujtahid may err, but the ruling is valid and binding until proven wrong.
This underscores the Hanafi view that zanni evidence is sufficient for practical law.

البحث الأول في كتاب الله فصل في المشترك والمؤول وعلى هذا قلنا: لا يجب النظير في جزاء الصيد؛ لقوله تعالى: فَجَزَاء مِثْلُ مَا قَتَلَ مِنَ النعمه الآية؛ لأن المثل مشترك بين المثل صورة، وبين المثل معنى وهو القيمة، وقد أُريد في الجسم من حيث المالية المثلُ من حيث المعنى بهذا النص في قتل الحمام والعُصْفُور ونحوهما بالاتفاق، فلا يراد المثلُ وهو القيمة المذكور من حيث الصورة؛ إذ لا عموم للمشتَرَك أصلاً، فَيَسْقُطُ اعتبار الصورة لاستحالة الجمع. لا حقيقة ولا مجازا ثم إذا ترجّح بعضُ وجوه المشترك بغالب الرأي يصير مؤوَّلاً. في المثل لا يجب النظير إلخ أي خلقة، وقد قال بوجوبه الشافعي ومالك وأحمد وغيرهم له، ومحمد بن الحسن له من أصحابنا حيث قالوا: يجب النظير فيما له نظير في الخلقة، ففي الظبي الشاة، وفي الأرنب عناق، وعند إمامنا الأعظم له: يجب المثل معنى وهي القيمة، وبيانه إذا قتل المحرم صيداً فجزاؤه أن يقوم الصيد في المكان الذي قتل فيه، أو في أقرب المواضع إذا كان في بر فيقومه ذوا عدل ثم هو يخير، إن شاء ابتاع بها هدياً وذبحه إن بلغت هدياً، وإن شاء اشترى بها طعاماً ويتصدق على كل مسكين نصف صاع من بر، أو صاعاً من تمر أو شعير، وإن شاء صام على ما ذكر في موضعه. لا عموم للمشتَرَك : المراد بعموم المشترك: أن يشمل جميع معانيه، وهذا منعه الحنفية وجمهور الأصوليين وجميع أهل اللغة، وبعض المحققين من أصحاب الشافعي، وقال الشافعية وبعض الأصوليين: إن الأصل هو أن المشترك لا يدل إلا على معنى واحد ولكن يجوز أن يطلق على كل معانيه بطريق الحقيقة إذا صح الجمع بينهما . [ حاشية الشيخ أكرم الندوي: ص ٣٨] بغالب الرأي: أي الظن الحاصل بالقياس أو خبر الواحد أو القرائن الأخرى في النصوص، وأما مثال النقود في الحكميات فمبني على ما عرفت من أن المشترك لا يجب تعدد الوضع بل يكفيه تعدد المختلفات أيضاً ولو في معنى واحد من جهة اختلاف المصاديق أو تكثر الموارد أو غيرهما، والمراد بغالب نقد البلد أي بلد البائع لا المتبايعين: ما هو الأروج فيه والأرجح على غيره من الأثمان بالتعارف ومزيد الاستعمال وهو إحدى قرائن الإرادة وأمارتها، فيكون كالقياس والخبر في إيراث الظن، وقوله مختلفة أي مختلفة المالية، والمراد به: أن يكون الكل سواء في الرواج كذا في "الهداية". يصير مؤوَّلاً إلخ: المؤول مأخوذ من آل يؤل إذا رجع وأولته إذا رجعته وصرفته؛ لأنك متى تأملت في اللفظ وصرفته عما يحتمل من الوجوه المحتملة إلى وجه فقد رجعته إليه والمراد به ههنا هو المؤول من المشترك لا وحكم المؤَوَّل وجوبُ العَمْل به مع احتمال الخطأ. وذلك ومثاله: في الحكميَّات ما قلنا: إذا أطلق الثمن في البيع كان على غالب نقد البلد، تعيين غالب نقد البلد بطريق التأويل، ولو كانت النقود مختلفة فسد البيع؛ لما ذكرنا. وحمل الأقراء على في البلد بأن بين القدر دون الصفة من استحالة الجمع وعدم الرجحان الحيض، وحملُ النكاح في الآية على الوطء، وحمل الكنايات حال مذاكرة الطلاق على الطلاق من المشترك بين العقد والوطء عن الطلاق مذا القبيل، وعلى هذا قلنا: الدَّينُ المانع من الزكاة يصرف إلى أيسر أي التأويل المالين قضاء للدين. وفرَّع محمد محله على هذا فقال: "إذا تزوج امرأة على نصاب، وله نصاب من الغنم، ميهم من نصاب الزكاة المؤول مطلقاً فافهم مع احتمال الخطأ أما في تأويله؛ لأن التأويل لا يكون إلا بأمر ظني، وهو يستلزم احتمال الغلط؛ لأن المجتهد يخطئ ويصيب، وفي بعض النسخ لفظه "على" بدل "مع" لكن يكون "على" حينئذ بمعنى "مع" كما يقال : فلان بحر في العلوم على صغر سنه أي مع صغر سنه. بر سر بالله فسد البيع إلخ لاستحالة الجمع وعدم الرجحان إلا إذا بين أحدهما فحينئذ ترتفع الجهالة المفضية إلى النزاع، والفساد إنما كان لأجلها وحمل الأقراء أي في آية التربص وهو قوله تعالى: ﴿وَالْمُطَلَّقَاتُ يَتَرَبَّصْنَ بِأَنْفُسِهِنَّ ثَلاثَةَ قُرُوع الآية. [الشافي: ص ٦٣] وحمل الكنايات: أي في قول الرجل لزوجته: أنت بائن. [الشافي: ص ٦٣] من هذا القبيل أي من قبيل التأويل؛ وذلك لأن القروء مشترك بين الحيض والطهر والنكاح مشترك بين الوطء والعقد، وألفاظ الكنايات كالبائن مثلاً مشترك يحتمل أن يكون من البيان أو من البين، فإذا حمل القروء على الحيض والنكاح على الوطء وكنايات الطلاق حال مذاكرة الطلاق على أن المراد بها الانقطاع من وصلة النكاح كان ذلك تأويلاً كذا في "الشروح". وعلى هذا: أي أن المحتمل للشيئين يصرف إلى أحد محتمليه بدليل يفيد غلبة الظن كما في الألفاظ المشتركة. إلى أيسر المالين: أي إذا كان لرجل نصب من الدراهم والدنانير والعروض والسوائم، وعليه دين يستغرق بعضه، يصرف أولاً إلى النقود؛ لأن قضاء الدين منه أيسر ; لعدم الاحتياج فيه إلى البيع، ثم إلى العروض؛ لأنها عرضة، ثم إلى السوائم؛ لأنها فاضلة عن الحاجة، ثم إلى المشغول بحاجة كدار السكنى وثياب البدن، ودواب الركوب، وعبيد الخدمة وغيرها.
The first research on the Book of Allah. Chapter on the Common (Mushtarak) and the Interpreted (Mu'awwal). And upon this we said: The likeness (al-nazir) is not obligatory in the penalty for hunting, due to the statement of Allah Most High: 'So the penalty is a like (mithl) of what he has killed from the cattle' the verse; because mithl is common (mushtarak) between likeness in form and likeness in meaning which is value, and it has been intended by this text in the body regarding wealth the likeness in meaning, in killing a pigeon, sparrow, and the like by agreement, so the likeness mentioned (which is value) is not intended in terms of form, because there is no generality for the common term (mushtarak) at all, so consideration of form drops due to impossibility of combination. Neither as a reality nor as a metaphor. Then if some aspects of the common term become preponderant by predominant opinion, it becomes interpreted (mu'awwal). Regarding mithl: 'the likeness is not obligatory' etc., meaning physical form; and al-Shafi'i, Malik, Ahmad and others held its obligation, and Muhammad ibn al-Hasan among our companions also held it, as they said: the physical likeness is obligatory for what has a physical likeness; for a gazelle, a sheep; for a rabbit, a young goat; and according to our great Imam (Abu Hanifa), the likeness in meaning is obligatory, i.e., its value. Its explanation: when a muhrim kills game, his penalty is to appraise the game in the place where it was killed, or in the nearest place if it was in a desert; two just persons appraise it; then he has a choice: if he wishes, he purchases a sacrificial animal with that amount and slaughters it if it reaches the value of a sacrificial animal; if he wishes, he purchases food and gives in charity to each poor person half a sa' of wheat or one sa' of dates or barley; if he wishes, he fasts as mentioned in its place. 'No generality for the common term': the meaning of generality of the common term (mushtarak) is that it includes all its meanings; and this is denied by the Hanafis, the majority of usulists, and all linguists, and some researchers among the followers of al-Shafi'i; and the Shafi'is and some usulists said: the principle is that the common term (mushtarak) does not indicate except one meaning, but it is permissible to use it for all its meanings by way of reality if combination between them is possible. [Hashiyat al-Shaykh Akram al-Nadwi: p. 38] 'By predominant opinion': i.e., the zann (conjecture) obtained by qiyas, khabar al-wahid, or other contexts in the texts. As for the example of currencies in legal matters, it is based on what you have known that mushtarak does not require multiplicity of wad' (linguistic assignment), but rather multiplicity of different things is sufficient for it, even in one meaning from the perspective of difference of applications or multiplicity of instances or other aspects. The intended meaning of 'the predominant currency of the country' is that of the country of the seller, not of the two contractors: whatever is the most circulated and preponderant over other prices by custom and extensive use, which is one of the contexts of intention and its indicators, so it is like qiyas and khabar in producing zann. And his statement 'different' means different in value, and the intent is that all are equal in circulation, as in al-Hidayah. 'It becomes mu'awwal' etc.: mu'awwal is derived from aala ya'ulu if it returns, and awwaltuhu if I returned it and diverted it; because when you reflect on the word and divert it from the possible aspects to one aspect, you have returned it to it, and the intended meaning here is the mu'awwal from the common term (mushtarak), not... The ruling of the mu'awwal is the obligation of acting upon it with the possibility of error. And that is so. And its example in legal matters is what we said: when the price is mentioned absolutely in a sale, it is upon the predominant currency of the country; specifying the predominant currency of the country is by way of interpretation (ta'wil). If the currencies were different, the sale becomes invalid due to what we mentioned. And the interpretation of 'quru' in the verse as menstruation, and the interpretation of 'nikah' in the verse as intercourse, and the interpretation of kinayat (allusions) during the discussion of divorce as divorce, from what is common between marriage and intercourse, about divorce of this category. And upon this we said: the debt that prevents zakat is paid from the easiest of the two assets as a means of fulfilling the debt. And Muhammad derived a branch upon this and said: 'If a man marries a woman on a nisab, and he has a nisab of sheep, it is from the nisab of zakat, the mu'awwal absolutely, so understand.' With the possibility of error regarding his interpretation; because interpretation (ta'wil) is only by a zanni matter, which entails the possibility of error because the mujtahid errs and hits. In some copies, the word 'ala is used instead of ma'a, but then 'ala in this context means ma'a, as it is said: 'He is a sea of knowledge 'ala (despite) his young age,' i.e., ma'a (with) his young age. 'The sale becomes invalid' etc., due to impossibility of combination and lack of preponderance unless one of them is specified, then the ambiguity leading to dispute is removed; invalidity is due to it. And the interpretation of 'quru' is in the verse of waiting period, which is His statement: 'And divorced women shall wait for three quru' the verse. [al-Shafi: p. 63] And the interpretation of kinayat: i.e., the saying of a man to his wife: 'You are ba'in' [al-Shafi: p. 63] is from this category, i.e., from the category of interpretation; because quru' is common between menstruation and purity, and nikah is common between intercourse and marriage, and the words of kinayat like 'ba'in' for example are common, possibly meaning separation or distance. So when quru' is interpreted as menstruation, and nikah as intercourse, and kinayat of divorce during discussion of divorce as intended for separation from the marriage bond, that is interpretation (ta'wil), as in the commentaries. 'And upon this': meaning that what is possible for two things is diverted to one of its possibilities by a proof that yields predominant conjecture (ghalabat al-zann), as in common words. 'To the easiest of the two assets': i.e., if a man has dinars, dirhams, goods, and grazing animals, and he owes a debt that consumes some of them, he first pays from cash, because paying the debt from it is easier due to no need for sale; then from goods because they are at hand; then from grazing animals because they are surplus to need; then from items occupied by need such as a residential house, body garments, riding animals, and service slaves, and other things.
Source pages p. 31

Commentary
This passage from Usul al-Shashi is a foundational exposition of two critical concepts in Hanafi usul al-fiqh: al-mushtarak (the homonym) and al-mu'awwal (the interpreted meaning). The author opens with a fiqhi application: the penalty for a muhrim (person in ihram) who kills game. The Quranic verse (al-Ma'idah 5:95) says 'fa-jaza'un mithlu ma qatala min an-na'am.' The word 'mithl' is mushtarak—it can mean similarity in form or similarity in value. The Hanafi position, following Imam Abu Hanifa, holds that it means value, not a physical likeness. This is because mushtarak has no general coverage (la 'umum lil-mushtarak), meaning it cannot simultaneously refer to all its possible meanings. Since combining both form and value is impossible, the form is dropped and value is deemed intended by preponderance of evidence (ghalabat al-dhann). The passage then notes the ikhtilaf: Shafi'i, Malik, Ahmad, and even Muhammad ibn al-Hasan among the Hanafis hold that the physical likeness is obligatory for animals that have a physical counterpart (e.g., a sheep for a gazelle). But the relied-upon Hanafi position is value, with detailed rules for substitution by food or fasting. The text then defines mushtarak and the principle that it cannot be used for all meanings simultaneously except by way of metaphor (majaz), though some Shafi'is allow it if combination is possible. The concept of mu'awwal is introduced: when one meaning of a mushtarak becomes preponderant due to a contextual indicator (qarīna), the word becomes 'interpreted' and must be acted upon, even though there remains a possibility of error. Examples include: interpreting the price in a sale by the predominant currency of the country; interpreting 'quru'' in the verse on 'iddah as menstruation (Hanafi view, as opposed to Shafi'i who interpret as purity); interpreting 'nikah' in a certain verse as intercourse; and interpreting kinayat (allusions) during discussions of divorce as actual divorce. Another application: a debt that prevents zakat should be paid from the most readily available assets (e.g., cash before goods). Muhammad al-Shaybani derives a branch ruling: if a man marries a woman for a specific nisab and he has a nisab of sheep, that falls under the mu'awwal as well. The commentary emphasizes that all these rulings are based on the usul principle that mushtarak is not general and that interpretation (ta'wil) is based on predominant zann (conjecture), which inherently carries the possibility of error—hence the mujtahid may be wrong. The passage concludes with practical details of how to determine the easiest asset for debt repayment. Throughout, the author maintains a consistent Hanafi usul framework, distinguishing it from the Shafi'i school on the nature of mushtarak and the method of interpretation.

Key Terms
المؤول (al-mu'awwal): A mushtarak word after one of its meanings has been given preponderance (tarjih) by a contextual indicator, making it the intended meaning. Acted upon despite possibility of error.
القرء (al-qur'): A word mushtarak between menstruation (hayd) and purity (tuhr). In the verse on iddah, Hanafis interpret it as menstruation.
غالب نقد البلد (ghalib naqd al-balad): The predominant currency of a country, determined by custom and frequent use. Used to interpret absolute mention of price in contracts.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on a sale where the price is mentioned absolutely and the country has multiple currencies of equal circulation but different values?
A) The sale is valid; the price is interpreted as the predominant currency.
B) The sale is invalid (fasid) due to ambiguity.
C) The sale is valid, and the buyer can choose the currency.
D) The sale is suspended until both parties specify.

Key Takeaway
Mu'awwal – the interpreted meaning of a mushtarak – is acted upon in all practical rulings, though it is based on predominant conjecture (zann) and may carry a possibility of error.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
intermediate
6 min
The Interpreted Term (Mu'awwal): Definition, Ruling, and Examples
Defines mu'awwal as mushtarak given preponderance; its ruling is wajib al-amal with error possibility

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define mu'awwal, state its ruling (wajib al-amal with error possibility), and distinguish it from mufassar.

Core Idea
A common term interpreted by speculative evidence is binding but fallible.

In this passage, we encounter a core concept of Hanafi usul: the mu'awwal—a common term (mushtarak) whose meaning is given preponderance by speculative (ẓannī) evidence. Understanding mu'awwal is essential for grasping how mujtahids derive rulings from ambiguous texts while acknowledging the possibility of error. This lesson dissects the definition, ruling, and illustrative examples provided in the text.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal definition of mu'awwal
From the text, extract the definition: al-mu'awwal is a common term (mushtarak) whose one meaning has been given preponderance by a speculative evidence (dalīl ẓannī). Contrast this with mufassar, which uses certain evidence from the speaker.
The text does not give an explicit definition but the contrast with mufassar implies it.
2
State the ruling of acting upon mu'awwal
The text says: 'wa ḥukm al-mu'awwal wujūb al-‘amal bihi ma'a iḥtimāl al-khaṭa'. This means it is obligatory to act upon it, but with the possibility of error.
The possibility of error arises because the evidence is probabilistic.
3
Analyze the examples to see how preponderance is established
Examine the examples: currency in sale (dominant currency), interpretation of 'quru'' as menses, 'nikāḥ' as intercourse, and kinayah in divorce. In each, a ẓannī evidence (custom, context) gives preponderance to one meaning.
These examples show mu'awwal in action across different fiqh chapters.
4
Distinguish mu'awwal from mufassar
If the speaker provides a certain clarification (bayān qāṭi‘), the term becomes mufassar and must be acted upon with certainty (yaqīnan). Example: specifying 'from Bukhara currency'.
This distinction determines the epistemic weight of the ruling.

المؤول مطلقاً فافهم مع احتمال الخطأ أما في تأويله؛ لأن التأويل لا يكون إلا بأمر ظني، وهو يستلزم احتمال الغلط؛ لأن المجتهد يخطئ ويصيب، وفي بعض النسخ لفظه "على" بدل "مع" لكن يكون "على" حينئذ بمعنى "مع" كما يقال : فلان بحر في العلوم على صغر سنه أي مع صغر سنه.
بر سر بالله
فسد البيع إلخ لاستحالة الجمع وعدم الرجحان إلا إذا بين أحدهما فحينئذ ترتفع الجهالة المفضية إلى النزاع، والفساد إنما كان لأجلها وحمل الأقراء أي في آية التربص وهو قوله تعالى: ﴿وَالْمُطَلَّقَاتُ يَتَرَبَّصْنَ بِأَنْفُسِهِنَّ ثَلاثَةَ قُرُوع الآية. [الشافي: ص ٦٣] وحمل الكنايات: أي في قول الرجل لزوجته: أنت بائن. [الشافي: ص ٦٣] من هذا القبيل أي من قبيل التأويل؛ وذلك لأن القروء مشترك بين الحيض والطهر والنكاح مشترك بين الوطء والعقد، وألفاظ الكنايات كالبائن مثلاً مشترك يحتمل أن يكون من البيان أو من البين، فإذا حمل القروء على الحيض والنكاح على الوطء وكنايات الطلاق حال مذاكرة الطلاق على أن المراد بها الانقطاع من وصلة النكاح كان ذلك تأويلاً كذا في "الشروح". وعلى هذا: أي أن المحتمل للشيئين يصرف إلى أحد محتمليه بدليل يفيد غلبة الظن كما في الألفاظ المشتركة. إلى أيسر المالين: أي إذا كان لرجل نصب من الدراهم والدنانير والعروض والسوائم، وعليه دين يستغرق بعضه، يصرف أولاً إلى النقود؛ لأن قضاء الدين منه أيسر ؛ لعدم الاحتياج فيه إلى البيع، ثم إلى العروض؛ لأنها عرضة، ثم إلى السوائم؛ لأنها فاضلة عن الحاجة، ثم إلى المشغول بحاجة كدار ،السكنى وثياب البدن، ودواب الركوب،
وعبيد الخدمة
وغيرها.
